801 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. Children's Servs. Div.


CA A82612


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


140 Ore. App. 429; 914 P.2d 1123; 1996 Ore. App. LEXIS 511



April 17, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 9212-08179. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Robert P. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the decedent's estate representative and mother, appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), in favor of defendants, Children's Services Division and youth caregiver, for the alleged wrongful death of her son. Plaintiff argued that the trial court erred in allowing the jury to consider the comparative fault of the decedent's parents in contributing to decedent's death.


OVERVIEW: Based on her contention that the person seeking recovery was decedent's personal representative and not a beneficiary entitled to recover for wrongful death, the mother reasoned that the alleged fault of her and her husband in contributing to her son's death could not be compared with defendants' fault under Or. Rev. Stat. § 18.470. She argued that the affirmative defenses that sought to make that comparison should be stricken for failure to state a defense. Defendants contended that the mother's pretrial motion to strike the defenses was insufficient to preserve the issue. The court found that although the mother could have raised the issue at trial she was not required to do so to preserve the issue and found that the conduct of beneficiaries would be considered in determining whether contributory negligence barred a wrongful death claim. Consequently, the jury could properly consider the alleged fault of the mother and her husband because they were beneficiaries who were entitled to recover damages. It followed, then, that the trial court properly denied the mother's motion to strike the affirmative defenses that raised the fault of the mother and her husband as a defense.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court finding that the affirmative defense of the mother and her husband's comparative fault was not barred was affirmed in the mother's suit, brought as the personal estate representative, for the wrongful death of her son while in defendants' custody.

 

802 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Belzons


CA A85212


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


140 Ore. App. 198; 915 P.2d 428; 1996 Ore. App. LEXIS 515


June 28, 1995, Argued and submitted  
April 17, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] DCR9411265. Appeal from District Court, Clackamas County. Robert R. Selander, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered a plea of no contest and was convicted of menacing, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.190, a class A misdemeanor. He was placed on probation for two years. In seeking reversal of his conviction from the District Court, Clackamas County (Oregon), defendant argued that the district court lacked jurisdiction to enter any judgment and, thus, any sentence imposed was in excess of that allowed by law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised the jurisdictional defect for the first time on appeal. The court upheld the judgment and sentence of the district court. Because defendant pleaded no contest, under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050(1), his right to direct appeal was statutorily limited to challenging the district court's disposition as exceeding the maximum allowable by law or as unconstitutionally cruel and unusual. Based on defendant's argument, the court's inquiry was limited to whether his sentence exceeded the maximum allowable. Defendant was correct that the district court lacked jurisdiction because his crime was committed after a statutory amendment removed class A misdemeanors from the jurisdictional authority of district courts. However, the court found that his sentence did not exceed the maximum allowable by law. A two-year probationary sentence was within the statutory limits and within the sentencing limits of the district court under Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.010(4). Although defendant purported to challenge an "excessive sentence," the essence of his argument was that the conviction itself was improper. Review of that issue was not available under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

 

803 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Warren v. Baldwin


CA A84209


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


140 Ore. App. 318; 915 P.2d 1016; 1996 Ore. App. LEXIS 546


October 20, 1995, Argued and submitted  
April 17, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CV 93-0289. Appeal from Circuit Court, Umatilla County. Robert B. Abrams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions to enter judgment granting post-conviction relief on manslaughter conviction; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Umatilla County (Oregon), which denied his petition for postconviction relief, after he was convicted of manslaughter in the second degree, Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.125, assault in the fourth degree, Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.175, and felon in possession of a firearm, Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.270.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of, inter alia, manslaughter in the second degree after a gun he struck a third party with discharged and fatally shot the victim. He sought postconviction relief, alleging inadequate assistance of counsel and challenging the lawfulness of his sentence. On appeal from the denial of his request for relief, defendant argued that his alleged drug dealing, his prior convictions and his assaultive behavior toward others were irrelevant to whether he was reckless in later striking the third party with a handgun. His counsel's failure to object to the evidence, he argued, was therefore deficient and prejudicial. The unchallenged use of irrelevant evidence to prove recklessness was likely to have influenced the jury to decide the manslaughter charge on an improper basis. Defense counsel's failure to object was therefore not a judgment call, but rather a failure to exercise reasonable professional skill and judgment. The error had a tendency to affect the result of the prosecution on the manslaughter charge. Defendant was therefore denied adequate assistance of counsel under Or. Const. art. I, § 11, and was entitled to relief from his manslaughter conviction.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to grant defendant postconviction relief on his manslaughter conviction. Defense counsel's failure to object to the prosecutor's improper remarks prejudiced defendant and had a tendency to affect the result of the prosecution.

 

804 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Richter


CA A89416


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


140 Ore. App. 1; 914 P.2d 703; 1996 Ore. App. LEXIS 413



March 27, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Richter, 323 Ore. 691, 920 P.2d 550, 1996 Ore. LEXIS 549 (1996)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 95CR0718. Appeal from Circuit Court, Coos County. Richard L. Barron, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, upon a guilty plea, by the Circuit Court, Coos County (Oregon) for delivery of a controlled substance. After sentencing, defendant submitted an affidavit of indigence, but the trial court denied his motions for appointment of counsel for an appeal and a transcript of the trial court proceedings at state expense. The issue on appeal was whether he was entitled under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.500(3) to the transcript.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court denied his motions, defendant moved the court, apparently pursuant to Or. R. App. P. 3.05(5), for court-appointed counsel and a transcript at state expense. The court appointed counsel under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.500(1) but denied the motion for a transcript with leave to renew upon showing that a transcript was necessary. The due process and equal protection clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment did not mandate an unconditional entitlement to a free transcript. The court denied the motion because defendant had not made a sufficient showing under § 138.500(3) that the transcript was material and necessary. Section 138.500(3) required counsel to make a showing of some possible contention for appeal that required a transcript to assess. Because defendant pled guilty and was given a presumptive sentence pursuant to the sentencing guidelines, the cognizable issues on appeal were very limited and, correspondingly, appellate counsel's window of opportunity to identify a contention for appeal was small. Since appellate counsel could not suggest a reasonably cognizable contention to raise on appeal, there was no necessity for a transcript at state expense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for a trial transcript at state expense.

 

805 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Shelby v. Board of Parole & Post-Prison Supervision


CA A87773


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


140 Ore. App. 102; 915 P.2d 414; 1996 Ore. App. LEXIS 428


January 11, 1996, Argued and submitted  
March 27, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Judicial Review from Board of Parole and Post-Prison Supervision. On respondent's motion to dismiss filed April 10, 1995.



DISPOSITION: Petition for judicial review dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed an order of respondent Board of Parole and Post-Prison Supervision (Oregon), which deferred his parole release date by two years. The Board filed a motion to dismiss the inmate's appeal.


OVERVIEW: The Board deferred the inmate's parole release date by two years because he suffered from a mental or emotional disturbance which rendered him a danger to the health and safety of the community. The inmate appealed the Board's decision, contending that former ORS § 144.335(2), which provided that the Board's order postponing an inmate's release date due to the inmate's emotional problems was final and not subject to review, was unconstitutional. The court held that (1) judicial review, as defined by ORS § 144.335, described direct review of an order in a contested case; (2) ORS § 144.335(2), which was enacted after he committed his crime, did not violate the ex post facto protections of the state and federal Constitutions because the law did not enhance the inmate's punishment; (3) both before and after the amendment to ORS § 144.335, the standard for deferral of an inmate's release date was whether the inmate had a mental or emotional disturbance and the only change to the law had been procedural, i.e. whether inmates could directly appeal deferral determinations to the appellate court; and (4) ORS § 144.335(2) was constitutional and barred review of the inmate's petition.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the inmate's petition for judicial review.

 

806 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sumerlin


CA A84062


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


139 Ore. App. 579; 913 P.2d 340; 1996 Ore. App. LEXIS 390


April 27, 1995, Argued and submitted  
March 20, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 10-93-09367. Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Ann Aiken, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences by the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon) for assault in the second degree, assault in the third degree, reckless driving, driving under the influence of intoxicants, and two counts of reckless endangering, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 163.175, 163.165, 811.140, 813.010, 163.195, respectively.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was intoxicated and speeding, he rear-ended another vehicle and injured the occupants. Defendant pleaded guilty and was given consecutive sentences. Defendant claimed that the convictions and sentences should have been merged because they involved one episode. The State claimed that because defendant pleaded guilty, he waived the merger issue. The court held that the appeal, the convictions, and the sentences were proper. The merger issue was appealable because of an issue whether the sentence complied with Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.222(4)(a) and the anti-merger statutes, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 161.062, 161.067, overruled contrary judicial precedent. The court overruled State v. Anderson, 119 Or. App. 23, 849 P.2d 548 (1993). The reckless endangering and reckless driving convictions were properly not merged because they involved different factual elements in that the former charge required a substantial risk of physical harm. The two counts of reckless endangering were properly not merged because they involved two discrete victims. The consecutive sentences were authorized by Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.123(4)(a) because intoxication was only required for one of the convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

 

807 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Schuch v. Board of Parole & Post-Prison Supervision


CA A85111


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


139 Ore. App. 327; 912 P.2d 403; 1996 Ore. App. LEXIS 255


April 27, 1995, Argued and submitted  
February 28, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Judicial Review from Board of Parole and Post-Prison Supervision.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner parolee sought judicial review of a decision of the Board of Parole and Post-Prison Supervision (Oregon), which established a one-year minimum term of supervision and declared him a "predatory sex offender" under Or. Rev. Stat. § 181.585, former § 181.507.


OVERVIEW: The parolee was convicted of sodomy and sexual abuse for molesting his five- and seven-year-old half brothers. His sentence was suspended and he was placed on five years' probation. Five months later, he was convicted of first-degree sexual abuse for molesting an eight-year-old neighbor boy, and his probation was revoked. He was sentenced to concurrent terms of a maximum of 10 years on the prior sodomy convictions, five years on the prior sexual abuse convictions, and five years on the last conviction. Nearly six years later, after an exit interview and upon reconsideration, the Board affirmed the parolee's release date and imposed a minimum of 12 months' supervision. An accompanying order included a specific finding that the parolee was a "predatory sex offender" under former Or. Rev. Stat. § 181.507. On appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that the Board did not abuse its discretion to determine whether the parolee was such an offender where a corrections department assessment gave him a "high" risk level and that his Fourteenth Amendment due process rights were not violated because the labeling of him as a predatory sex offender did not constitute punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Board's decision establishing a supervision term and declaring the parolee a "predatory sex offender."

 

808 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Davidson v. Board of Parole & Post-Prison Supervision


A86212


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


139 Ore. App. 289; 911 P.2d 973; 1996 Ore. App. LEXIS 201


August 31, 1995, Argued and submitted  
February 21, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Opinion Modified on Allowance of Reconsideration March 27, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ore. App. LEXIS 424.


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review from Board of Parole and Post-Prison Supervision.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought judicial review of an order of the Board of Parole and Post-Prison Supervision (Oregon), which imposed a 12-month term of supervised parole, followed by unsupervised parole for the balance of his sentence.


OVERVIEW: According to petitioner, at the time his crime was committed, he was subject to former ORS 144.310 applied, which provided for discharge from his sentence after six months or a year of parole. The court agree with the Board that petitioner's argument proceeded from a false premise, namely, that he was subject to ORS 144.310 at the time his crime was committed. At the time of the crime, a different statute, former ORS 144.305 (repealed by Or. Laws 1993, ch. 680, § 7), applied, and that statute provided for parole extending for the entire term of an offender's sentence. ORS 144.305 applied to all crimes committed after December 4, 1986. Petitioner's was such a crime. ORS 144.310 remained "on the books" only as to crimes committed before the effective date of ORS 144.305. The amendment to ORS 144.310 in 1987 was to replace the term "Corrections Division" with the term "Department of Corrections." Or. Laws 1987, ch. 320, § 61. There was no repeal, express or implied, of ORS 144.305 and the Board properly applied it. The Board's order did not violate the ex post facto clause of either the state or federal constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

 

809 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Jackson v. Fred Meyer, Inc.


CA A85672


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


139 Ore. App. 222; 911 P.2d 957; 1996 Ore. App. LEXIS 203


December 14, 1995, Argued and submitted  
February 21, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 94CV0266. Appeal from Circuit Court, Coos County. Robert F. Walberg, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee challenged a decision of the Circuit Court, Coos County (Oregon), which granted summary judgment dismissing her personal injury claim against defendant former employer. The trial court held that the employee's exclusive remedy was under the Workers' Compensation Act. The employee argued that the Act violated Or. Const. art. I, § 10 because it took away her common law remedy against the employer.


OVERVIEW: The employer accepted the employee's workers' compensation claim. The employee sent the employer's insurer medical bills for treatment that occurred after she was declared medically stationary. The parties entered into a disputed claim settlement. The employee then filed the instant action. She argued that Or. Rev. Stat. § 656.018(2) violated Or. Const. art. I, § 10 because, at common law, she was only required to prove that the employer's negligence was a substantial factor in causing her injury; under § 656.018(2), she was required to prove the employment was the major contributing cause of her condition. However, the employee did not provide the court with an actual factual setting that properly framed the issue of the statute's constitutionality. Under Or. Const. art. I, § 10, the legislature had the authority to limit common law remedies as long as it did not leave the injured party entirely without a remedy. The employer accepted compensability of the original injury and paid the employee to settle her later claims. Thus, the employee was not denied a remedy because she was unable to prove that her work-related injuries were the major contributing cause of her condition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the employer.

 

810 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Petrie v. City of Lake Oswego


CA A90367


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


139 Ore. App. 8; 911 P.2d 346; 1996 Ore. App. LEXIS 100


November 22, 1995, Argued and submitted  
February 7, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] LUBA No. 95-094. Judicial Review from Land Use Board of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a memorandum decision of the Oregon Land Use Board of Appeals, which affirmed the land use decisions of respondent city.


OVERVIEW: The city made land use decisions against petitioner. The Board, in a memorandum decision, affirmed the decisions. Upon review, the court determined that it could consider petitioner's assignments of error, which challenged putative errors in the city proceedings rather than errors by the Board because the Board's decision took the form of a memorandum decision. Furthermore, the Board had similar authority to that possessed by appellate courts to summarily dispose of cases before them, which included, under Or. Rev. Stat. § 197.835(16) the authority to decide cases without opinion. Although the Board did not have blanket authority to decide cases without explanation, petitioner provided no specific basis for reversal or remand to the Board. Finally, the court determined that neither Or. Rev. Stat. § 197.835(16) nor the Board's interpretation of it violated Or. Const. art. I, § 20 or U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Board's decision.

 

811 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Maynard


CA A81182


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


138 Ore. App. 647; 910 P.2d 1115; 1996 Ore. App. LEXIS 93


November 21, 1994, Argued and submitted; resubmitted in banc March 8, 1995  
January 24, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 10-92-06551. Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. F. Gordon Cottrell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Convictions on Counts 2, 3, and 4 reversed; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon) that convicted him of furnishing obscene materials to minors in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.065(1)(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of endangering the welfare of minors and furnishing obscene materials to minors. He appealed the count of furnishing obscene materials to minors on the ground that § 167.065(1)(a) was an unconstitutional restriction on free expression under Or. Const. art. I, § 8 and under U.S. Const. amend. I, and the court reversed. The court found that it could sever a portion of the statute previously found to be unconstitutional and could independently consider the remaining provisions. It determined that the prohibitions against furnishing materials to minors depicting sexual conduct or excitement violated the Oregon Constitution because the statute was an impermissible content-based statute directed solely at prohibiting certain communication with minors. The statute failed to identify either expressly or by inference an actual effect or harm that it was designed to prevent. The court also concluded that the statute did not represent a modern version of a historically established exception to the Oregon Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for furnishing obscene materials to minors but affirmed the conviction for endangering the welfare of minors.

 

812 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Keenan v. Maass


CA A84950


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


138 Ore. App. 576; 911 P.2d 331; 1996 Ore. App. LEXIS 94


August 24, 1995, Argued and submitted  
January 24, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 94-C-11097. Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Richard D. Barber, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon) dismissing a writ of habeas corpus pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 34.680(1) for failing to state or establish a claim for habeas corpus relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate petitioned for a for a writ of habeas corpus, alleging that he suffered from severe headaches, jaw aches and migraines stemming from Temporomandibular Joint Dysfunction (TMJ), and that he had a severe overbite that caused his teeth to grind and chip off. The inmate alleged that the dismissal of the writ of habeas corpus by the trial court was erroneous on the grounds that his affidavit raised genuine issues of material fact as to the propriety of habeas corpus relief. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the inmate's affidavit recited that two different dentists at two different correctional facilities told him that until his severe overbite was "repaired" his teeth would continue to chip and break off. Thus, the inmate's affidavit raised a genuine issue as to whether he had been afforded such care for his overbite as was "reasonably available" under the circumstances. Moreover, the court determined that there was a material issue of fact as to whether plaintiff was diagnosed as having a TMJ condition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court dismissing the inmate's writ of habeas corpus.

State v. Jurado


CA A85616

State v. Orton


CA A84481


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


137 Ore. App. 339; 904 P.2d 179; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 1459


July 21, 1995, Argued and submitted  
October 18, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 9401-40386. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Charles B. Guinasso, Judge (Trial). Dorothy M. Baker, Judge (Demurrer).



DISPOSITION: Conviction for violation of ORS 163.750 reversed; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Circuit Court of Multnomah County. (Oregon) for violating a court-issued stalking protective order (SPO) in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.750.


OVERVIEW: Defendant violated the SPO by coming into the visual or physical presence of the petitioner. He was charged with violating § 163.750, two counts of unlawful possession of a firearm in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.250, and two counts of carrying a loaded firearm, in violation of a city ordinance. He pleaded guilty to unlawful possession of a firearm and was convicted of violating the SPO. The remaining charges were dismissed. On appeal, the court reversed his conviction for violating the SPO. The court found that the question of defendant's pre-SPO issuance contacts were without legitimate purpose, within the meaning of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.738, was litigated in the prior SPO issuance proceeding. Yet, the court also found that the issues of whether defendant's post-SPO issuance contact with petitioner was without legitimate purpose, and whether "without legitimate purpose" as a component of a prosecution under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.750 was unconstitutionally vague, were not litigated or susceptible to litigation during the issuance proceeding. The court ruled that the term "without legitimate purpose," as incorporated within § 163.750, was unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for violating a court-issued stalking protective order.

816 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wheelon


CA A81165


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


137 Ore. App. 63; 903 P.2d 399; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 1397


April 18, 1995, Argued and submitted  
September 27, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CR 92-465(A) & (B). Appeal from Circuit Court, Yamhill County. John L. Collins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded on appeal; affirmed on cross-appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court, Yamhill County (Oregon), which suppressed evidence seized from two defendants charged with multiple counts of manufacture, delivery and possession of a controlled substance, Or. Rev. Stat. § 475.992, and with two counts of child neglect, Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.547. Defendants also claimed that a search warrant for their property was based upon a false affidavit of two informants.


OVERVIEW: A warrant was issued for a search based upon the affidavit of a state police officer, who stated that he had information from two citizen informants describing a large marijuana growing operation conducted by defendants. The property was searched by the police and members of the Oregon National Guard, and over 100 plants and paraphernalia were hauled away. The trial court found that the affidavit did not specify that the two informants saw the property at the same time and did not corroborate each other and that there was not probable cause to issue a warrant. On review, the court found that a lesser degree of proof was needed to establish the veracity of citizens without a connection to the crime being investigated, that cross-corroboration was not needed, and that the information in the affidavit met the lesser showing of reliability. The court reversed the suppression and found that the execution of the warrant was not unconstitutional because the Guard participated in it as part of an order to cooperate with a county interagency narcotics team.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which had suppressed the evidence seized in a search of defendants' property, and remanded. The court affirmed the trial court's decision on defendants' cross-appeal and ruled that the affidavit in support of the warrant was sufficient.

 

817 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anderson


CA A81744


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


137 Ore. App. 36; 902 P.2d 1206; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 1401


April 27, 1995, Argued and submitted  
September 27, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CM93-0524. Appeal from Circuit Court, Benton County. Robert S. Gardner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court, Benton County (Oregon), which convicted him of rape in the first degree, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.375, and of sodomy in the first degree, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.405. The basis of the conviction was the victim's incapacity to consent because of mental defect.


OVERVIEW: The victim was a mentally retarded and hearing-impaired 25-year old woman. At trial, defendant had sought to introduce evidence of statements that defendant had heard regarding the victim's sexual reputation. The trial court rejected the introduction of such statements, but it did allow evidence of specific instances of the victim's past sexual relationships with two other men and evidence that she frequented the tavern where she had met defendant and acted suggestively towards men there. On review, the court held that under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.325(3), defendant's generalized belief that the victim could consent to sexual relations was immaterial to his asserted state of mind; rather, to avoid culpability, defendant had to have shown that he did not know of the facts or conditions responsible for the victim's incapacity to consent. The court agreed with the State that the victim's alleged reputation for promiscuous sexual activity was immaterial to that inquiry. Rather, what was critical was defendant's awareness of the victim's mental retardation. The court rejected defendant's remaining assignments of error and affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's rape and sodomy convictions.

 

818 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Warden


CA A83201


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


136 Ore. App. 268; 901 P.2d 900; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 1172


November 10, 1994, Argued and submitted  
September 6, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 93-40409. Appeal from District Court, Lane County. Lauren S. Holland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of an order of the District Court, Lane County (Oregon), which granted defendant's demurrer to a charge that he cast light from a motor vehicle while armed in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.663.


OVERVIEW: Defendant demurred to the charge on the grounds that § 166.663 was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The trial court concluded that § 166.663 was overbroad and unconstitutionally infringed on defendant's right to bear arms under Or Const. art I, § 27. The court held that the trial court erred in allowing defendant's demurrer because § 166.663 imposed a reasonable restriction that was directly aimed at the public's safety and welfare. It did not unreasonably infringe on defendant's right to bear arms. Section 166.663 regulated only the manner of possession, therefore, it was permissible legislation because it was directed to a specific public safety or welfare concern and did not unreasonably encroach on the constitutional right. Section 166.663 did not proscribe mere possession of a firearm. Only when an individual was casting artificial light from a motor vehicle was the manner of possession restricted. Defendant's facial vagueness challenge was not properly before the court, because § 166.663 did not implicate rights under the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order granting defendant's demurrer to the charge that he cast light from a motor vehicle while armed.

State v. Pelham


CA A81474


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


136 Ore. App. 336; 901 P.2d 972; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 1185


April 3, 1995, Argued and submitted  
September 6, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] DA 488069-9304. Appeal from District Court, Multnomah County. Anna J. Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the District Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which denied his motion to compel a television station (station) to release a videotape of his arrest, granted the station's motion to quash pursuant to Oregon's Media Shield Law, Or. Rev. Stat. § 44.510 et seq., and convicted him of trespass in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.565(2).


OVERVIEW: A police officer repeatedly asked defendant, a radio reporter, to leave a designated area. Defendant refused and continued to ask the police officer questions. A television cameraman videotaped defendant's arrest for trespass. Defendant filed a motion to compel production of the videotape. He argued that the videotape contained material, favorable evidence that proved that he complied with the police officer's orders to leave. The station filed a motion to quash on the basis of a strict policy of nondisclosure for unpublished information and on the basis of the Media Shield Law. The trial court denied defendant's motion to compel, granted the station's motion to quash, and convicted defendant of trespass. The court affirmed. The court held that defendant's claimed error was reviewable because he was not required to inform the station, which was not a party to the criminal action, of the appeal. Defendant was not deprived his right to compulsory process under Ore. Const. art. I, § 11 because he failed to establish that the station's videotape contained evidence that was material and favorable to him because the cameraman did not film defendant's actions that led to his arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to deny defendant's motion to compel production of the station's unpublished videotape and affirmed his trespass conviction.

 

820 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


DeVaux v. Presby


CA A81932


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


136 Ore. App. 456; 902 P.2d 593; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 1197


January 11, 1995, Argued and submitted  
September 6, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 9301-00199. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Charles B. Guinasso, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant homeowners appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), on a jury verdict entered in favor of plaintiff guest for personal injuries.


OVERVIEW: The guest sought damages for injuries suffered when he was attacked by another person who lived on the homeowner's land. The jury found for the guest. The court affirmed on appeal and found that there was sufficient evidence of the landowner's ownership and control of the premises to allow the matter to be submitted to the jury. The court also found that the trial court properly excluded a consideration of the fault of the guest, under Or. Rev. Stat. § 18.845. Having found no merit to the guest's claim that the landowners failed to preserve their objections, the court considered whether the jury properly awarded damages for the guest's loss of earning capacity. The court found that pursuant to § 18.560(2)(a), loss of future earning capacity was an objectively verifiable monetary loss, under the category of economic damage. The court found no merit to the landowners' claim that loss of future earnings would fail the standard of proof under common law. The court found that evidence that the guest had sustained permanent injury and that this injury affected his ability to do his job was sufficient to permit him to submit the issue of loss of future earning capacity to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court on a jury verdict that awarded the guest damages for personal injuries.

Starr v. Eccles


CA A82721


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


136 Ore. App. 30; 900 P.2d 1068; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 1104


December 16, 1994, Argued and submitted  
August 2, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 93-787. Appeal from Circuit Court, Baker County. Milo Pope, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for entry of judgment dismissing stalking protective order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent former patient sought review of a decision of the Baker County Circuit Court (Oregon), which prohibited the former patient from intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly having any contact with petitioner psychologist. The former patient alleged that the stalking statutes, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 163.730-163.753, were unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The patient asserted that the stalking statutes, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 163.730-163.753, which were the basis of the stalking protective order, were unconstitutionally vague because they failed to provide guidelines for an officer or a court to determine what a "legitimate purpose" was. The patient asserted that the stalking statutes violated his right of access to public places under Or Const. art. I, §§ 8, 26, and U.S. Const. amend. I, XIV. Further he argued that the statutes were unconstitutionally vague and overbroad, deprived him of his federal rights of equal protection and due process, and violated other constitutional provisions. The court determined that under the unique circumstances of the case, the issue of whether the words "legitimate purpose" were unconstitutionally vague was sufficiently preserved for review. The court found that the phrase "legitimate purpose" was unconstitutionally vague. The court determined that because the phrase was unconstitutionally vague, both the officer and the trial court were without authority to enter a stalking protective order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court, which had granted a stalking protective order to the psychologist in an action brought against the former patient.

 

822 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Juarez-Godinez


CA A78977


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


135 Ore. App. 591; 900 P.2d 1044; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 1094


February 28, 1994, Argued and submitted  
July 26, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 92C-21343. Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Rodney W. Miller, Judge. Resubmitted in banc June 8, 1995.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the order of the Marion County Circuit Court (Oregon) granting defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized from the vehicle he was driving pursuant to a search warrant.


OVERVIEW: The vehicle defendant was driving was stopped for speeding. There were other people in the vehicle. The police officer arrested defendant for not having a driver's license. The officer requested a canine unit, which arrived 45 minutes later. The dog sniffed the outside of the vehicle and "alerted" at the passenger door. A search warrant was obtained and drugs were found in the vehicle. The trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress. On appeal, the court affirmed. Defendant had a privacy interest in the vehicle's contents because they did not "announce" their presence by an odor that the officer could smell while outside of the vehicle. Therefore, the use of the dog constituted a search. None of the officer's observations, including the facts that the vehicle contained several air fresheners, three occupants were well-dressed, and it was traveling to Tacoma, justified a reasonable suspicion that the vehicle contained drugs. Therefore, the warrantless search by the dog violated defendant's rights under Or. Const. art. I, § 9.


OUTCOME: The order suppressed the evidence seized from the vehicle defendant was driving was affirmed.

Fence v. Jackson County


CA A88196


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


135 Ore. App. 574; 900 P.2d 524; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 1099


June 15, 1995, Argued and submitted  
July 26, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 94-137. Judicial Review from Land Use Board of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: On petition, invalidation of ordinance sections 620.04(b) and 620.05(b) reversed, and otherwise affirmed; on cross-petition, reversed and remanded for consideration of constitutional issues, and otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner county sought review of a decision by the Land Use Board of Appeals (Oregon), which remanded an enactment of an ordinance by the county that added provisions regulating outdoor "mass gatherings." Respondent citizen also cross-appealed the decision.


OVERVIEW: The citizen contended that some or all of the county's regulations were preempted by Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 433.735 to 433.770, that the regulations were inconsistent with the Federal Religious Freedom Restoration Act of 1993, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000bb et seq., and that they violated religious and communicative protections of the federal and state constitutions because of their effects on Native American ceremonies and activities in which the citizen wished to engage. One issue was whether the land use board had jurisdiction. The court found that the regulations had a significant nexus with land use and that the land use board had jurisdiction. However, although the county could regulate the subject, its regulations could not be inconsistent with the statutes. The court held that a portion referring only to application processing fees was not invalid for that reason alone and that Or. Rev. Stat. § 433.755(1) mandated a case-by-case assessment as part of the permit application process. The court further ruled that consideration of the constitutional issues the citizen raised was necessary, and remanded for the land use board to address the parts of the ordinance that remained viable.


OUTCOME: On the county's petition, the invalidation of two county ordinance sections was reversed, but the other portion of the land use board's decision was otherwise affirmed. On the citizen's cross-petition, the land use board's decision that the remainder of the ordinance sections were still viable was reversed and remanded for consideration of constitutional issues but was otherwise affirmed.

825 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Merrill


CA A81412 (Control), CA A81413 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


135 Ore. App. 408; 899 P.2d 712; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 998


October 27, 1994, Argued and submitted  
July 12, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Dismissed as Improvidently Allowed March 21, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ore. LEXIS 25.


PRIOR HISTORY: 92-1081, 92-1082. Appeal from Circuit Court, Columbia County. Donald L. Kalberer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged pretrial orders from the Circuit Court, Columbia County (Oregon), which, in different cases, granted defendants' demurrers to identically worded two-count indictments. Each defendant had been charged with the offenses of unlawful delivery of a controlled substance (marijuana) and unlawful possession of a controlled substance (marijuana) in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 475.992(1), (4).


OVERVIEW: Defendants demurred to their indictments on the grounds that count one included two or more crimes not separately pleaded and that count two failed to include an adequate allegation concerning the amount of marijuana allegedly possessed. The trial court granted the demurrers. On appeal, the State alleged that count one did not charge defendants with multiple offenses, but that it alleged one offense and two alternative offense-subcategory facts that did not need to be alleged in separate counts. In reversing the circuit court's orders, the court ruled that when an indictment properly alleged the elements of an underlying offense, the inclusion of alternative grounds for enhancing the sentence did not create additional offenses. The trial court erred in concluding that count one alleged multiple offenses. The court also ruled that where the language of a statute plainly drew a distinction between the elements of a crime and an exception or proviso, the State did not have to allege that the exception did not apply. Accordingly, the State was not required to allege that the felony-offense exception did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders from the circuit court and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Chakerian


CA A83155 (Control), CA A83173, CA A83174, CA A83175 and CA A83176) (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


135 Ore. App. 368; 900 P.2d 511; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 955


April 27, 1995, Argued and submitted  
June 28, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] C93-07-34971, C93-07-34975, C93-07-34970, C93-07-34972 and C93-07-34973. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Janice R. Wilson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Multnomah County (Oregon) sustaining defendants' demurrers to charges of riot. The trial court concluded that the statute underlying the charges, Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.015, was unconstitutionally overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with violating the anti-rioting statute, Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.015. They demurred, asserting, inter alia, that § 166.015 was unconstitutional in that it was directed to the content of expression and did not fall within any historically recognized exception to the free speech protections of Or. Const. art. I, § 8; the statute was overbroad in that it criminalized expression protected under Or. Const. art. I, § 8; and the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The trial court rejected defendants' arguments that the § 166.015 was content-driven and unconstitutionally vague, but ultimately allowed their demurrers on the ground that the statute was overbroad. The State argued that § 166.015 was not susceptible to facial overbreadth challenges, by way of demurrer, based on Or. Const. art. I, § 8. The court determined that Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.015 did not expressly refer to speech. Nor was expression the only means by which the statute could be violated. Consequently, the court concluded that § 166.015 was not susceptible to an overbreadth challenge. The court also held that the phrase "grave risk of public alarm" in § 166.015 was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

Malek v. Atlantic Mut. Cos.


CA A85235


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


135 Ore. App. 205; 897 P.2d 350; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 970


April 19, 1995, Argued and submitted  
June 28, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 9405-03528. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Michael H. Marcus, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer of respondent injury victim's employer challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which enforced an arbitration award, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 36.350, in favor of the victim pursuant to the underinsured motorist coverage of the insurance policy of the victim's employer.


OVERVIEW: The victim was injured in an automobile accident with an underinsured motorist and made a claim against the insurer. The victim's attorney requested arbitration then brought an action under § 36.350 to enter the favorable award as a judgment. The insurer filed an exception to the award and a motion for a jury trial, arguing that if judgment were entered it would be denied its right to a jury trial on the damage issue. The trial court denied the exception and motion and entered judgment. The insurer was correct that, to the extent that Or. Rev. Stat. § 754.504(10) was mandatory and made an arbitration award binding against a nondemanding party, it was unconstitutional. However, if the parties agreed to arbitrate, the insurer had not been deprived of its right to a jury trial. Whether the parties agreed to arbitration was a question of fact and the court, on appeal, was bound by the trial court's findings with evidentiary support. The trial court had found that the insurer did not arbitrate under statutory compulsion with supportive evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which enforced an arbitration award in favor of the victim. The trial court did not err in denying the insurer's exception and motion for a jury trial.

 

828 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Zackheim v. Forbes


CA A84090


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


134 Ore. App. 548; 895 P.2d 793; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 779; 23 Media L. Rep. 2396


March 27, 1995, Argued and submitted  
May 24, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 93C 12528. Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Duane R. Ertsgaard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attorneys appealed the decision from the Circuit Court of Marion County (Oregon), which granted summary judgment to defendants, the State and state officials, and denied the attorneys' motion for summary judgment in their suit challenging the constitutionality of Or. Rev. Stat. § 802.220(7) and Or. Rev. Stat. § 802.224, two statutes related to public access to accident reports.


OVERVIEW: The attorneys sought the accident reports to solicit clients. They contended that the denial of the use of the records violated their free speech rights to communicate with clients. The appellate court reversed, holding that the two statutes were invalid. Collectively, the two statutes held that accident records were not privileged except that they could not be used for "commercial purposes." The use of the records for such purposes was a crime. The court found that, first, while the State could restrict the use of private information, the records were public information. Next, the court found that the statutes violated Or. Const. art. I, § 8 as content-based restrictions on speech. While content-based restrictions were not per se unconstitutional, the State failed to show that the restriction fell within an historical exception. There was no historical exception for the use of public records for commercial purposes. The State's argument that the statutes protected the privacy rights of victims was rejected because the statutes permitted the media to have access to the records and allowed access to anyone as long as the records were not used for commercial purposes.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment to the State and the denial of summary judgment to the attorneys was reversed and remanded.

Lind v. Allstate Ins. Co.


CA A83422


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON

May 17, 1995, FILED

PRIOR HISTORY: 9312-08151. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Lee Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Multnomah County (Oregon), which enforced an arbitration award in favor of plaintiff insured on her claim against the insurer for uninsured motorist coverage. The insurer sought a jury trial pursuant to Or. Const. art. I, § 17.


OVERVIEW: The insured was injured in a motor vehicle collision with an uninsured motorist. The insurer denied her uninsured motorist claim, and the insured obtained an arbitration award pursuant to procedures outlined in the insurance contract. The insurer refused to pay the award, and the insured filed an action to enforce the award. The trial court ordered enforcement, but on appeal, the court reversed and remanded. Stat. § 742.504(10), by rendering uninsured motorist arbitration awards binding against nondemanding parties, violated Or. Const. art. I, § 17. Therefore, the insurance contract provision making arbitration awards nonbinding if they are for an amount greater than the financial responsibility law limit for bodily injury was enforceable and properly invoked by the insurer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment enforcing the arbitration award and remanded for a jury trial.

State v. Weber


CA A82239


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


134 Ore. App. 390; 895 P.2d 331; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 756


January 31, 1995, Argued and submitted  
May 17, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CR1-1832. Appeal from District Court, Deschutes County. Barbara A. Haslinger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered a guilty plea in the District Court, Deschutes County, Oregon, to a charge of driving under the influence of intoxicants (DUII) in violation of ORS 813.010. After an amended citation was filed, defendant was convicted pursuant to his plea agreement. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: When defendant was arrested for DUII he was issued a uniform traffic citation and complaint that mistakenly charged him with an infraction instead of a Class A misdemeanor. Defendant pleaded guilty to DUII as charged in exchange for the dismissal of other charges. At a sentencing hearing, defendant argued that because he pleaded guilty to DUII charged as an infraction, the court could not impose the Class A misdemeanor sentence mandated by ORS 813.010(4). The state submitted its sentencing memorandum and an amended citation that properly charged defendant with DUII as a Class A misdemeanor. Defendant did not object. Defendant was sentenced pursuant to DUII as a Class A misdemeanor. Defendant appealed. Defendant had entered a guilty plea, so the only issue on appeal, pursuant ORS 138.050(3)(a), was whether the sentence exceeded the maximum allowable by law. The sentence did not exceed that allowed under the properly amended citation for a Class A misdemeanor, so the sentence was affirmed. Defendant had waived his argument that the sentence exceeded the maximum allowed for an infraction because he had not objected to the amended citation or withdrawn his plea.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

832 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Norris-Romine


(CA A83772 (Control), CA A83931 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


134 Ore. App. 204; 894 P.2d 1221; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 679


February 6, 1995, Argued and submitted  
May 3, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 9422M; Q9400667M; Z9400670M. Appeal from Circuit Court, Jackson County, and Circuit Court, Washington County. Mark Schiveley, Judge, Jackson County, and Donald R. Letourneau, Judge, Washington County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two separate cases consolidated on appeal, the State appealed the dismissal of accusatory instruments charging defendants with violations of stalking protective orders in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 163.747 and 163.750 by the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Oregon) and the Circuit Court of Washington County (Oregon).


OVERVIEW: Defendants were accused of violating stalking protective orders. One defendant was charged under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.747 for violating a protective order issued under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.735. The other defendant was charged under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.750 for violating a protective order issued under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.738. The trial courts dismissed the charges after finding that the statutory definition of the phrase "without legitimate purpose," as a component of the crime of violating a stalking protective order, was unconstitutionally vague. Affirming the trial court's rulings, the court held that the term "legitimate purpose," as used in the stalking statutes, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 163.730(7), 163.732, 163.735, and 163.738, and as in pari materia with Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 163.747 and 163.750, was unconstitutionally vague. The statutes on their face did not tell a person of ordinary intelligence what was encompassed within the term "legitimate purpose." Because they failed to do so, the statutes gave no warning as to what conduct had to be avoided. They provided no guidance to the trier of fact and permitted ad hoc judgments as to what was legitimate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the charges against defendants.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Yamhill County (Oregon), granted summary judgment in favor of appellee, the Aeronautics Division of the Oregon Department of Transportation, in a wrongful death action initiated by appellant, the estate of a passenger who died in an airplane crash. The estate filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was a passenger in a small airplane that crashed shortly after taking off from an airstrip, which was located at a restaurant and resort facility. The decedent's estate initiated a wrongful death action against the division. United Employer Benefit Corp. v. Department of Ins. & Fin.


CA A77744


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


133 Ore. App. 477; 892 P.2d 722; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 515

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff marketing agency challenged an order from the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which entered a directed verdict for defendants, Oregon Department of Insurance and Finance (DIF) and purchaser, on its takings claims under the federal and state constitutions. The marketing agency also challenged a directed verdict for the purchaser on the marketing agency's claim for intentional interference with business relations.

The marketing agency brought an action against DIF and the purchaser for inverse condemnation and argued that the purchaser had tortiously interfered with its business relations by asking DIF to restrain its marketing abilities. There was no evidence that the purchaser suggested or knew of the press release before it was issued.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the entry of directed verdicts on the marketing agency's claims against DIF and the purchaser because their actions did not amount to an unconstitutional taking, and the purchaser did not intentionally interfere with the marketing agency's business relations.

Shipp v. County of Multnomah


CA A82275


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


133 Ore. App. 583; 891 P.2d 1345; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 518


September 28, 1994, Argued and submitted  
March 22, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 9212-08289. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Joseph F. Ceniceros, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which dismissed on the merits his petition for a review of the decision of the county's board of commissioners. He had added the petition to the declaratory judgment action he filed against respondent county.


OVERVIEW: The property owner inherited eight tax lots. The real property taxes were delinquent, and the county foreclosed on the lots. An owner could redeem the property in accordance with Or. Rev. Stat. § 312.120. The county's ordinance extended the statutory time period of redemption. The owner claimed that with regard to two lots the county had not followed the proper procedures, and he was not given the opportunity to repurchase the lots. The board of commissioners denied his appeal, and he filed suit for a declaratory judgment. The circuit court permitted him to amend his action to include a petition for review of the commissioners' decision. The matter was dismissed on the merits. On appeal, the court held that the circuit court never had jurisdiction over the issue. The only mechanism available to the owner was a petition for review in conformance with Or. Rev. Stat. § 34.030, not a declaratory judgment action. The petition for review was not timely because it was not filed within 60 days of the commissioners' decision. The circuit court had no authority to permit the amended complaint to relate back to the date of the original complaint, which was filed within the 60-day period.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment but noted that the lower court had never obtained jurisdiction over the matter.

 

836 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Withers v. State


CA A85596


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


133 Ore. App. 377; 891 P.2d 675; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 438


February 6, 1995, Argued and submitted  
March 8, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 94CV0074ST. Appeal from Circuit Court, Deschutes County. Stephen N. Tiktin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff students appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Deschutes County (Oregon), for defendant state, ruling that the statutes challenged by the students did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, Or. Const. art. VIII, § 3, or Or. Const. art. I, § 20. The students challenged the education funding scheme that involved 1991 Or. Laws 780, §§ 3, 8, 29, 1991 Or. Laws 162, § 8, and parts of 1991 Or. Laws 61.


OVERVIEW: The students filed an action seeking a declaration that certain education funding measures violated state and federal constitutions. They claimed that they were denied educational opportunities that were available in other districts not subject to the limitation. The trial court entered judgment on the pleadings for the state, and the court affirmed the judgment below. Funding measures were constitutional under Or. Const. art. VIII, § 3, if they provided a minimum of educational opportunities in a district and permitted districts to exercise local control over additional provisions. The constitution did not require equal school funding, only that the education system was uniform in the prescribed courses of study and educational progression. Equality of resources from district to district was not required. The court also ruled that even if the funding system discriminated against a true class under Or. Const. art. I, § 20, there was a rational basis for the discrimination. The legislature's choice of a temporary and gradual phasing in of new funding measures was properly designed to avoid the harm that full and immediate implementation of the new statutory scheme would have caused.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of judgment on the pleadings for the state in the students' action for a declaratory judgment that certain education funding measures violated the state and federal constitutions.

 

837 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Solomon


CA A81504


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


133 Ore. App. 184; 890 P.2d 433; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 386


August 5, 1994, Argued and submitted  
February 22, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 93-20068. Appeal from District Court, Lane County. Lauren Holland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the District Court of Lane County (Oregon), following a jury trial, of initiating a false report to the police in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.375. Defendant appealed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant objected to the trial court's exclusion of two tape recorded conversations from the person who allegedly provided defendant with the incorrect information about a crime. At trial, his sole theory for the admissibility of the recordings was that they were hearsay that showed his state of mind at the time he made the report to the police. The trial court found that the tapes were not relevant and that they were hearsay that did not come within the exception argued by defendant. On appeal, defendant abandoned his position that the tapes showed his state of mind. He argued that the tapes were not hearsay or, if they were, that they came within Or. Evid. Code § 804(3)(f), the catch-all exception to the hearsay rule. The court rejected the challenge, finding that defendant did not just fail to make a particular argument as to the admissibility of the evidence. Instead, his position did not give the trial court any opportunity to make the findings required under § 804(3)(f) and did not provide the opposing party with an opportunity to present competing arguments. Under those circumstances, defendant's argument was not in a posture capable of review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment.

Billings v. Gates


CA A83424


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


133 Ore. App. 236; 890 P.2d 995; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 402


November 14, 1994, Submitted on record and briefs  
February 22, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 94-02-26238-M. Appeal from Circuit Court, Malheur County. F. J. Yraguen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate challenged a dismissal of his petition for a writ of habeas corpus against defendant correctional institution.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff petition alleged that the institution's shoes had no arch support, that arch supports were medically necessary for him, and that the institution would not provide the arch supports to him. The trial court issued an order directing the institution to show cause why the writ should not have been allowed. The institution's response included both a memorandum of law and an affidavit by a nurse at the institution. Based on the institution's response to the show cause order, the court denied the petition as meritless. On appeal, the court held that the trial court's consideration of factual materials in the context of the show cause order was erroneous and could not be reconciled with the statutory framework requiring the show cause order. The statutory scheme contemplated that factual issues would be litigated after the writ issued and the return and replication were made. Further, the court found that the inmate stated a sufficient claim in his petition in that he alleged that the lack of arch supported left him unable to walk, that arch supports were available through the commissary, and that notwithstanding his indigency, the institution refused to supply the supports.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause to the trial court.

State v. Upton

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Douglas County. William Lasswell, Judge. No. 90CR1969FE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a sentence of life without the possibility of parole that was imposed by the Circuit Court, Douglas County (Oregon) following her plea of guilty to a charge of aggravated murder, a violation of ORS 163.095. Defendant, who stipulated to the sentence while reserving her right to appeal it, claimed that the sentence violated Article I, § 40, of the Oregon Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to plea negotiations, defendant pleaded guilty to aggravated murder. Under a plea agreement, defendant stipulated to a sentence of life without the possibility of parole as described in ORS 163.105(1)(b), reserving the right to appeal the constitutional issue of whether the sentence was legal under Article I, § 40, of the Oregon Constitution. The trial court accepted the plea agreement and defendant sought review of the sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the sentence was not subject to review. The court reasoned that review was precluded under ORS 138.122(2)(d) because the sentence was a stipulated sentence within the meaning of ORS 135.407. The court held that defendant's purported reservation of the right to review of the sentence did not confer upon the court the authority to review it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Pollard


CA No. A77376


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


132 Ore. App. 538; 888 P.2d 1054; 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 93


April 28, 1994, Argued and submitted; November 9, 1994, Resubmitted In Banc  
January 25, 1995, Decided  
January 25, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied May 16, 1995 (321 Or 138).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Timothy P. Alexander, Judge. No. C920219CR.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court, Washington County (Oregon), which convicted him for murder by abuse under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.115(1)(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his conviction should be reversed because his statements to police officers were not voluntary. The court agreed and held that a confession or admission was deemed to be involuntary unless the State affirmatively showed that it was voluntarily made. The State had to prove voluntariness by a preponderance of the evidence. The court held that the State failed to meet its burden. The court further held that the error in admitting defendant's statement was not harmless. The court held that the admittance of defendant's statement was not harmless because there was not substantial and convincing evidence of guilt and little likelihood that the error affected the verdict. The court held that although there was substantial and convincing evidence that defendant had assaulted his son on various occasions before June 19, 1991, defendant's statements to the police that he had shaken his son on that date provided the final link to his death.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for a new trial.

State v. Stoneman


CA No. A70085


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


132 Ore. App. 137; 888 P.2d 39; 1994 Ore. App. LEXIS 1960


August 12, 1992, Argued and submitted; August 8, 1994, Resubmitted In Banc  
December 28, 1994, Decided  
December 28, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Allowed April 25, 1995 (321 Or 94).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Malheur County. F. J. Yraguen, Judge. No. 90-12-5153-C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court, Malheur County (Oregon), which sustained defendant's demurrer to an indictment under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.680 for paying to obtain a videotape and magazine that allegedly depicted sexually explicit conduct by a child under 18 years of age, on the ground that § 163.680 violated Or. Const. art. I, § 8.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for buying a videotape and magazine that allegedly depicted sexually explicit conduct by a child under 18 years of age in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.680 (1987), which made it illegal to pay or give anything of value to obtain or view that material. The trial court sustained defendant's demurrer to the indictment. On appeal, the court affirmed because § 163.680 regulated speech within the meaning of Or. Const. art. I, § 8 and it improperly focused on content rather than the harmful effects it sought to ameliorate. In addition, the state failed to show that § 163.680 fell within any historical free speech exception, such as perjury, solicitation, or verbal assistance in crime, some forms of theft, forgery, and fraud. Furthermore, there was no basis for a territorial foundation for an historical exception and the posited historical exception was to undefined to include § 163.680. The court declined to make a special constitutional exception for a child pornography law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that sustained defendant's demurrer to an indictment for paying to obtain a videotape and magazine that allegedly depicted sexually explicit conduct by a child under 18 years of age.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), denying his petition for declaratory relief. The inmate sought a declaration that the visitation rules established by the Department of Corrections were unconstitutional. The opposing parties included the Director of the Department, the Superintendent of the state penitentiary, and the superintendent of a women's correctional center.

The trial court entered a judgment in favor of the Department. On appeal, the court held that because the inmate was directly challenging the visitation rules of the Department, Oregon Administrative Procedures Act review was exclusive and the inmate was precluded from obtaining declaratory relief. Accordingly, it stated, the trial court lacked jurisdiction to consider the request by the inmate for declaratory relief.


OUTCOME: The court remanded with instructions to dismiss.

GTE Northwest v. Public Util. Comm'n


CA No. A81647


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


130 Ore. App. 637; 883 P.2d 255; 1994 Ore. App. LEXIS 1490


September 6, 1994, Argued and submitted  
October 19, 1994, Decided  
October 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Allowed December 20, 1994 (320 Or 492).


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review of Administrative Rules. No. 93-852.



DISPOSITION: Rules held valid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner local telephone company challenged certain rules of respondent, Public Utility Commission of Oregon (PUC), which required local telephone exchange companies (LECs) to offer collocation to enhanced service providers (ESPs) in their areas.


OVERVIEW: Or. Admin. R. 860-35-020(8), Or. Admin. R. 860-35-070(5), and Or. Admin. R. 860-35-110 required the local telephone company to offer collocation to ESPs, such as respondent telecommunications corporation. The PUC's rules required that the local telephone company allow each ESP to occupy a portion of the local telephone company's property for ESP equipment. The local telephone company facially changed the rules, claiming that they effected a taking under Or. Const. art. I, § 18 and under U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV. The court held that the rules were valid because collocation did not constitute a permanent physical occupation when the local telephone company had some control over the duration of the occupation, pursuant to Or. Admin. R. 860-35-110(4)(f). Further, Or. Admin. R. 860-35-110(4)(a) vested the local telephone company with some control over the extent of the occupation when there was no existing space for collocation. Moreover, the rules did not offend the traditional rights to possess property and to exclude others from the use of it. Therefore, it followed that the rules, on their face, did not violate Or. Const. art. I, § 18 or U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV.


OUTCOME: The court held that the PUC's rules requiring LECs to offer collocation to ESPs were valid.

Association of Oregon Loggers v. Department of Ins. & Fin.


CA No. A78305


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


130 Ore. App. 594; 883 P.2d 859; 1994 Ore. App. LEXIS 1495; 1995 OSHD (CCH) P30,842


December 6, 1993, Argued and submitted  
October 19, 1994, Decided  
October 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied December 27, 1994 (320 Or 493).


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review of Administrative Rules.



DISPOSITION: Rules held valid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 1873.400, petitioners, timber and logging organizations, sought review of certain rules issued by respondent Oregon Occupational Safety and Heath Division of the Department of Insurance and Finance. Petitioners alleged that the statements of need and of fiscal impact in the rules were inadequate to satisfy Or. Rev. Stat. § 183.335(2)(b)(B), (D) and that the rules exceeded their statutory authority.


OVERVIEW: The Division promulgated new rules to implement their authority under Or. Rev. Stat. ch. 654 to regulated health and safety in employment in the state. Petitioners challenged the new rules on numerous grounds, including that the Division exceeded its constitutional authority and its statutory authority. The court reviewed the new rules in detail and held that they were valid. The court held that the notice of proposed action was sufficient to alert interested persons that the rules might have some effect on them. The court also held that the agency's fiscal impact statement was adequate because the notice stated that it was uncertain of what impact the rules would have but stated historical trends and averages and thus, satisfied the requirement to use only available information to create that statement. The court ruled that the rules did not exceed the Division's statutory authority and were not unconstitutional vague. The court noted that the authority granted to an agency was quite board, and though an agency was not permitted to supplement an enabling statute by altering it through rules or created inconsistent rules, the rules at issue did not go beyond the enabling statutes.


OUTCOME: The court held that the rules were valid and did not modify them.

State v. Zelinka


CA No. A72874


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


130 Ore. App. 464; 882 P.2d 624; 1994 Ore. App. LEXIS 1440


July 27, 1993, Argued and submitted  
October 5, 1994, Decided  
October 5, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied January 24, 1995 (320 Or 508).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Polk County. Charles E. Luukinen, Judge. No. 90P-3292.



DISPOSITION: Conviction for criminal mistreatment affirmed; remanded for entry of a corrected judgment merging convictions of murder by abuse and for resentencing; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court, Polk County (Oregon), which following a jury trial convicted him of three counts of murder by abuse, Or. Rev. Stat. 163.115(1)(c), and criminal mistreatment and sentenced him to life imprisonment with a mandatory minimum term of 25 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted kicking his toddler daughter the night before she died. The court remanded for merger of the convictions for murder by abuse because there was only one victim and one statute violated and for resentencing. Affirming the judgment otherwise, the court held that the use of acts committed before § 163.115(1)(c) was enacted to prove a pattern of assault or torture did not violate state and federal ex post facto clauses because the crime was not completed until after the statute was enacted. The court found that the state constitution required Miranda-like warnings when a defendant was in "full custody" or the setting was "compelling" and that the federal Constitution required warnings when his freedom was significantly restrained. The court determined that defendant was entitled to warnings when he was escorted to the police station after he had confessed to kicking his daughter because the officers should have recognized the circumstances as "compelling," that he was adequately warned and knowingly and voluntarily waived his rights, and that continued questioning after he asked for counsel was constitutionally permissible because the request was limited.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for criminal mistreatment and remanded the matter for merger of the murder by abuse convictions and for resentencing in accordance with the sentencing guidelines.

State ex rel. Juvenile Dep't v. Mitchell (In re Mitchell)

Rev. Stat. § 419.507(11).


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted that he was within the juvenile court's jurisdiction because he committed an act that, if committed by an adult, would have constituted sodomy in the first degree. The court rejected defendant's claims.
