State v. Rode


CA No. A74503


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


118 Ore. App. 665; 848 P.2d 1232; 1993 Ore. App. LEXIS 445


October 5, 1992, Argued and submitted; January 6, 1993, Resubmitted In Banc  
March 17, 1993, Decided  
March 17, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 12, 1993. Petition for Review Allowed July 27, 1993 (317 Or 271).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Multnomah County. David White, Judge pro tempore. No. DA454553.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which found defendant guilty of attempted assault and harassment, violations of Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.565(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with attempted assault in the fourth degree and harassment. At arraignment, the district attorney elected to try the cases as violations under Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.565(2). Defendant's motion for a jury trial was denied, and in a trial to the court, he was found guilty on both charges. Defendant argued that he was denied his constitutional right to a jury trial under the Or. Const. art. I, § 11 when the district attorney elected to try the cases as violations under Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.656(2). Specifically, defendant claimed that pre-trial procedures, community condemnation and the historical perception of assaultive behavior as a "crime," showed that assaultive behavior had "criminal characteristics" that precluded its prosecution without the constitutional safeguard of a jury trial. The court held that § 161.565(2) permitted conduct that could be prosecuted as a misdemeanor to have be prosecuted as a violation. Defendant's conduct was not a crime, and the prosecution of the conduct was not a criminal prosecution. Defendant had no right under Or. Const. art. I, § 11, to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding defendant guilty.

 

901 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bannister


CA No. A67680


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


118 Ore. App. 252; 846 P.2d 1189; 1993 Ore. App. LEXIS 181


May 4, 1992, Argued and submitted  
February 17, 1993, Decided  
February 17, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Kimberly C. Frankel, Judge. C No. 90-02-31285.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which convicted him of kidnapping in the first degree with intent to terrorize. ORS 163.235(1)(d) (Oregon).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's daughter accused him of sexual abuse and she was sent away to live with an aunt. Defendant took her away. He was stopped by police, and weapons were found in the car. A tape was also found on which defendant told his daughter that they were going to die. Defendant was convicted of kidnapping in the first degree with a firearm with intent to terrorize. The court affirmed. Evidence of the daughter's allegation of sexual abuse was properly admitted to show the states of mind of defendant and his daughter. It was the strongest evidence to rebut defendant's' testimony on his intent in taking the daughter away and why he made the threat. Further, the trial court limited the testimony to only the fact that the allegations had been made; the details were excluded. The fact that his first trial resulted in an acquittal on a charge of kidnapping with intent to cause physical injury and a hung jury on a charge of kidnapping with a firearm with intent to terrorize did not bar his second trial for the charge upon which the jury was hung. ORS 131.525(1)(b)(D) provided an exception to the bar of double jeopardy in such situation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

State v. Albee


CA No. A70830


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


118 Ore. App. 212; 847 P.2d 858; 1993 Ore. App. LEXIS 192


July 13, 1992, Argued and submitted  
February 17, 1993, Decided  
February 17, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 14, 1993. Petition for Review Denied May 25, 1993 (316 Or 528).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Columbia County. Berkeley A. Smith, Judge. No. 89-5321.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court, Columbia County (Oregon) convicted defendant of involvement in animal fighting in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.355. Defendant appealed by challenging the denial of his motions to dismiss and to suppress.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that § 167.355 was void for vagueness and, therefore, violated the federal Due Process Clause, and Or. Const. art. I, §§ 20, 21. Defendant contended that the provision making it a crime for a person to be present as a spectator at an exhibition of fighting or preparations thereto was vague, because "preparations thereto" was not defined by the statute and allowed a jury to define it. Defendant's concerns about the general application of the statute were irrelevant because his conduct clearly came within the statutory language. Defendant's challenge under federal law was essentially identical to his state law challenge. Therefore, it was rejected for the same reasons the state law claim was. Defendant contended that the affidavit was insufficient to support a finding of probable cause, because the evidence did not demonstrate the reliability of the information from the unnamed informant. However, it was shown that the informant had provided accurate information in the past that the informant's information was extensively corroborated and, because the conduct involved an ongoing activity, the information was not stale.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Hartrampf


CA No. A70906


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


118 Ore. App. 237; 847 P.2d 856; 1993 Ore. App. LEXIS 225


July 13, 1992, Argued and submitted  
February 17, 1993, Decided  
February 17, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 14, 1993. Petition for Review Denied May 25, 1993 (316 Or 528).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Columbia County. Berkeley A. Smith, Judge. No. 89-5707.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court, Columbia County (Oregon) convicting him for attempted involvement in animal fighting, contrary to Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 167.355 and 161.405. Defendant contended the statutes were unconstitutionally vague in contravention of the Federal Due Process Clause and Or. Const. art. I, §§ 20 and 21.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stipulated that he knowingly was among the spectators at a farm hosting a cockfighting event. On appeal, he made no mention of any constitutionally protected right such as free speech; thus, the only issue was whether defendant's conduct fell within the statutes' prohibitions. The court found that the statutes establishing the offense of attempted involvement in animal fighting were not unconstitutionally vague. In order to be convicted of an attempt to commit a crime, a person must have intentionally engaged in conduct that constituted a substantial step toward commission of the crime. A person of common intelligence could have discerned that defendant's conduct constituted a substantial step toward involvement in animal fighting.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Skyport Properties of Oregon, Ltd. v. Multnomah County Drainage Dist. No. 1


CA No. A65993


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


117 Ore. App. 427; 844 P.2d 909; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 2536


February 3, 1992, Argued and submitted  
December 30, 1992, Decided  
December 30, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 24, 1993. Petition for Review Denied March 23, 1993 (315 Or 643).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Irving M. Steinbock, Judge. No. A8902-00962.



DISPOSITION: On appeal, judgment for defendant Multnomah County Drainage District No. 1 reversed; on cross-appeal, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both plaintiff developer and defendant county drainage district sought review of the judgment and decisions by the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon). The developer alleged that the trial court impermissible foreclosed a statutory lien on it as the damages did not come within the lienable rights of Or. Rev. Stat. § 547.420. The district alleged that the trial court impermissibly dismissed its counterclaim for breach of contract.


OVERVIEW: The developer entered into an agreement with the county drainage district permitting the developer to install culverts in a slough and to build a road over it for access to a new development. The agreement provided that the developer would keep the culverts in good working order and if it failed to, the district could acquire a lien to the property under Or. Rev. Stat. § 547.420. The district also alleged that the developer orally agreed to construct a bridge if necessary. The culverts were installed but due to concerns of a flood, the district proposed removing the culverts and replacing it with a bridge. The district then sent a demand letter to clean the culverts. When the developer did not clean them, the district removed the culverts, built the new bridge, and filed a lien against the developer for the new bridge. The court affirmed the dismissal of the district's breach of contract counterclaim because the claim was based on the oral agreement that could only be the basis of an implied contract, but reversed the judgment for the lien. The court held that § 547.420 only permitted recovery for costs to clean a culvert, not for costs for a new bridge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the district's counterclaim against the developer for breach of contract, but reversed the trial court's judgment for the district on the developer's claim that the district impermissibly imposed a statutory lien on it.

State v. Rose


CA No. A69717


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


117 Ore. App. 270; 843 P.2d 1005; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 2425


August 28, 1992, Argued and submitted  
December 23, 1992, Decided  
December 23, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 10, 1993. Petition for Review Denied April 20, 1993 (316 Or 142).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Deschutes County. Thomas Mosgrove, Judge. No. 90CR0131TM.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Deschutes County (Oregon), insofar as it convicted him of one count of first degree rape, ORS 163.375, two counts of second degree rape, ORS 163.365, and one count of third degree rape, ORS 163.355. Defendant claimed that the State failed to prove venue in Deschutes County.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raped a mentally retarded girl while he took her for drives. She could not say where the crimes occurred and, after defendant was extradited from Tennessee to Deschutes County, he was tried for rape in that county. Appealing from his convictions, defendant claimed that he was entitled to an acquittal because the State failed to prove that the rapes were committed in Deschutes County, and further that ORS 131.325, which permitted his trial in the county to which he had been extradited, was unconstitutional. The court held that the State was not required to prove the county in which the rapes were committed as an element of the offenses, and that ORS 131.325 relieved the State of the burden of proving the county in which the offenses were committed because that county could not readily be determined. It further held that ORS 131.325 did not violate Or. Const. art. I, § 11, because the constitutional provision was intended to protect a defendant from being tried in an unfriendly neighborhood, away from his friends, witnesses, and neighborhood, and was not intended to shield him from trial where the county in which he committed his crimes could not reasonably be determined.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Darroch


CA No. A69371


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


117 Ore. App. 185; 843 P.2d 978; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 2400


March 5, 1992, Argued and submitted  
December 16, 1992, Decided  
December 16, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 10, 1993. Petition for Review Denied March 23, 1993 (315 Or 643).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Jack L. Mattison, Judge. No. 10-90-07719B.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon) for manufacture, delivery, and possession of a controlled substance under ORS 475.992(1)(a), (4)(a).


OVERVIEW: A search warrant was issued for defendant's residence. Marijuana plants and other evidence of the manufacture, delivery, and possession of marijuana were seized. The warrant was based on an affidavit by a police officer, who had talked with another officer. The other officer told the affiant about an unusual amount of nighttime traffic at defendant's residence and that all the windows but one were covered with black. The affidavit also stated that the residence used a large amount of electricity in comparison with other similar or larger houses. Affirming, the court determined there was a factual basis in the affidavit for the issuance of the search warrant. Although not all of defendant's windows were covered, the statement of someone other than the affiant could not be controverted under ORS 133.693. It did not matter that the inaccurate statement came from another police officer or police employee rather than an informant. Defendant's motion to suppress was properly denied. The affidavit contained sufficient facts to support the issuance of the warrant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Alsea Veneer, Inc. v. State


CA Nos. A68787 (Control), A68788 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON v. STATE


117 Ore. App. 42; 843 P.2d 492; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 2324


September 14, 1992, Argued and submitted  
December 9, 1992, Decided  
December 9, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Alsea Veneer's Petition for Reconsideration and State's Petition for Reconsideration Denied April 14, 1993. Both Petitions for Review Allowed May 25, 1993 (316 Or 527).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Rodney W. Miller, Judge. Nos. 88C-11289, 88C-11300.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employers sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which refused to certify them as a class in their action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief for breach of contract, impairment of contractual relations, and violation of due process against defendants, State of Oregon and workers compensation fund (state).


OVERVIEW: The state directed the transfer of $ 81 million from the workers compensation fund to the state general fund. The employers sought declaratory and injunctive relief, and sought certification as a class. The trial court denied such certification. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the employers were entitled to class certification because each of the considerations in Or. R. Civ. P. 32A, 32B weighed in favor of certification. There were questions relating to damages common to the class members, including the transfer's effect on dividends and premiums. The claims all arose from the same transaction and were based on the same contractual liability theory. Differences in damages could be resolved with the creation of subclasses under Or. R. Civ. P. 32G(2). A single adjudication was preferable to piecemeal litigation and potentially inconsistent awards. Although the class was large, administration would be less difficult than separate management of the claims of each policyholder. Finally, the claims of individual class members were not likely to be adequate to cover their litigation costs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court refusing to certify the employers as a class in their breach of contract action against the state, and remanded.

State v. Lawrence


CA No. A70304


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


117 Ore. App. 99; 843 P.2d 488; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 2325


March 9, 1992, Argued and submitted; October 14, 1992, Resubmitted In Banc  
December 9, 1992, Decided  
December 9, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 17, 1993. Petition for Review Allowed April 20, 1993 (316 Or 142).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Lincoln County. Thomas O. Branford, Judge. No. 903896.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for driving under the influence of intoxicants in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 813.010 by the District Court, Lincoln County (Oregon). Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress the results of his field sobriety tests and his responses to questions from the arresting officers made after the testing stopped.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was stopped for committing traffic violations, the stopping officer noticed that defendant appeared intoxicated and asked defendant to perform field sobriety tests, noting that any refusal would be used against him in a court. Defendant did not perform well on the tests and after they were done, but before his arrest and the giving of a Miranda warning, the officer asked defendant several questions about his level of intoxication. Some of his answers were incriminating. The trial court convicted defendant of driving while under the influence of intoxicants. The court reversed that conviction and remanded the case for a new trial. The court held that field sobriety tests were both constitutional and did not compel a defendant to be a witness against himself in violation of Or. Const. art. I, § 12, and U.S. amend. V because the tests did not significantly impair a defendant's rights and did not violate a legitimate expectation of privacy. However, the court held that the trial court should have suppressed the statements made by defendant to the officer after the tests had finished because there was a clear break from the tests to an unlawful interrogation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's conviction of defendant for driving under the influence of intoxicants and remanded the case for a new trial.

Krieger v. Just


CA No. A69602


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


117 Ore. App. 64; 843 P.2d 473; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 2328

December 9, 1992, Decided  
December 9, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Krieger's Petition for Reconsideration and Just's Petition for Reconsideration Denied March 17, 1993. Both Petitions for Review Allowed April 20, 1993 (316 Or 142).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Yamhill County. John W. Hitchcock, Judge. No. CV90-122.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver challenged an order from the Circuit Court, Yamhill County (Oregon), which granted defendant driver's motion for summary judgment concerning a suit filed by plaintiff for damages incurred as a result of a collision of his vehicle with that of defendant's.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a suit against defendant asserting that he had incurred damages resulting from a collision of his and defendant's vehicle. Defendant filed a motion for summary judgment on the basis that she was a public employee acting in the course and scope of her employment at the time of the accident and that pursuant to Or. Rev. The court also held that summary judgment was granted in error because a reasonable juror could have found that, despite the exercise of reasonable diligence, plaintiff did not discover until defendant's deposition was taken that defendant was traveling on school business at the time of the accident.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded a summary judgment in favor of defendant in plaintiff's suit for recovery of damages incurred as the result of an automobile accident between plaintiff and defendant.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), convicted defendant of possession, delivery, and manufacture of a controlled substance, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 475.992, an ORICO charge, and Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.720. Defendant was also convicted of theft in the first degree in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.055. Defendant appealed from the convictions.

Stat. § 132.550(7), and of the Oregon and United States Constitutions. The court found that the indictment was specific as to the periods of time when the offenses occurred and described each in detail; therefore the court held that denial of the motion to dismiss was not error.

Merrick v. Board of Higher Educ.


CA No. A60997


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


116 Ore. App. 258; 841 P.2d 646; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 2052


July 10, 1992, Argued and submitted  
November 12, 1992, Decided  
November 12, 1992, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Judicial Review of Administrative Rules.



DISPOSITION: Rules held valid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee filed a proceedings under Or. Rev. Stat. § 183.400 to determine the validity of Or. Admin. Rs. 580-22-050, 580-15-0101, 580-15-065, promulgated by respondent board of higher education.


OVERVIEW: Or. Rev. Stat. § 236.380 codified a measure adopted by the voters, which effectively repealed an executive order prohibiting discrimination based on sexual orientation. The board of higher education promulgated Or. Admin. Rs. 580-22-050, 580-15-0101, 580-15-065, to comport with the statute. The employee filed a proceeding under Or. Rev. Stat. § 183.400 to determine the validity of the rules. The board then amended its rules so that they were identical to rules in effect before the passage of the statute, prohibiting discrimination on the basis of sexual orientation. The court held the last-adopted rules valid. The statute violated Or. Const. art. I, § 8; therefore, the statute did not limit the board's authority to promulgate the rules that were adopted after the proceeding was filed. Speech and status in the context of the statute were inextricably intertwined. In the absence of speech or communicative expression of some kind, the nature of a person's sexual orientation would rarely be known. Thus, the statute's practical effect was to chill speech and other expression and to severely limit open communication, violation of Or. Const. art. I, § 8.


OUTCOME: The court held that administrative rules promulgated by the board of higher education prohibiting discrimination in employment on the basis of sexual orientation were valid, in the proceeding of the employee to determine the validity of the administrative rules.

 

912 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Goodwin v. State


CA No. A66807


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


116 Ore. App. 279; 840 P.2d 1372; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 2161


December 6, 1991, Argued and submitted; September 9, 1992, Resubmitted In Banc  
November 12, 1992, Decided  
November 12, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Opinion Withdrawn December 22, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ore. App. LEXIS 2132.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Grant County. R. T. Gooding, Judge. No. 90-05-162 CV.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Grant County (Oregon), which granted petitioner post-conviction relief. The circuit court held that, because Or. Const. art. VII (amended), § 5(2) mandated a seven-person grand jury, the prosecutor's action of excusing one of the grand jurors from attendance at the session in which evidence against petitioner was presented and an indictment returned against him rendered the indictment void.


OVERVIEW: The State contended that only five jurors need have been present at a grand jury meeting and that they were able to return an indictment if they unanimously concurred. The State argued that the prosecutor's conduct was a violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 132.110(3) and not a constitutional violation. Petitioner was entitled to post-conviction relief only if the violation of § 132.110(3) also constituted a constitutional violation. The express language of Or. Const. art. VII (amended), § 5(2) required that a grand jury consist of seven persons, but allowed five to find an indictment. A grand jury panel of five or six jurors might not always have reached the same conclusion as if there were seven members. Or. Const. art. VII (amended), § 5(2) promoted a deliberative process that allowed consideration of minority viewpoints, thereby insulating an accused from biased or overzealous prosecution. Thus, the court held that Or. Const. art. VII (amended), § 5(2) mandated that seven grand jurors hear and consider all of the evidence presented before a valid indictment could have been found. Petitioner was entitled to dismissal of the indictment because only six grand jurors heard the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment, which granted petitioner post-conviction relief.

 

913 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hayes


CA No. A72075


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


116 Ore. App. 287; 843 P.2d 944; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 2165


July 6, 1992, Argued and submitted  
November 12, 1992, Decided  
November 12, 1992, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Gregory G. Foote, Judge. No. 10-91-03977.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which convicted defendant of perjury, a violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.065. Defendant assigned error to the trial court's denial of his motion for judgment of acquittal. Defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence to convict him of perjury.


OVERVIEW: A perjury charge arose from defendant's testimony during his trial for sodomy committed against his grandchild. The State asked defendant on cross-examination whether he had ever been mean to her. Defendant responded: "I've never been mean to any of my kids. My grandkids or my kids, never, neither one. No sir." During defendant's perjury trial, the State called four of defendant's children and grandchildren to prove the falsity of his answer. The witnesses testified that they had been sexually abused by defendant. The court found defendant guilty. Defendant argued that his testimony was not a proper basis for a perjury charge because a person's expression of an opinion cannot form the basis of a perjury conviction without proof, beyond a reasonable doubt, that the witness did not hold that opinion, no matter how unreasonable the opinion might be to others. Reversing the conviction, the court found that a pedophile may not believe that his conduct is "mean" or, even, wrong. The court found that because the State presented no evidence that even remotely suggested that defendant did not sincerely believe that he had not been mean, it failed to prove a misrepresentation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment that convicted defendant of perjury.

Eugene v. Powlowski


CA Nos. A72083 (Control), A72084 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


116 Ore. App. 186; 840 P.2d 1322; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 2007


July 8, 1992, Argued and submitted  
November 4, 1992, Decided  
November 4, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Lane County. Darryl L. Larson, Judge. Nos. 91-50040, 91-50041.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of judgments from the District Court, Lane County (Oregon), which found them guilty of violating a municipal ordinance that prohibited honking an automobile horn for purposes other than as a reasonable warning in the State's case against them. Defendants claimed the ordinance violated their right to free expression under Or. Const. art I, § 8.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were found guilty of violating a municipal ordinance that prohibited honking an automobile horn for purposes other than as a reasonable warning. Defendants appealed. In reversing the trial court's order, the court held that the Eugene Municipal Code § 5.005(1)(b), which adopted Or. Rev. Stat. § 815.225 violated Or. Const. art. I, § 8. The court found that the ordinance was overbroad on its face and was not limited to circumstance that were a detriment to the public interest. The court determined that the ordinance was so broad that it made honking unlawful if a motorist honked as a friendly greeting to a bystander. The court noted that the ordinance was not limited solely to circumstances of noise or abuse that implicated the public interest. The court concluded that the ordinance regulated far more behaviour than the city argued it was intended to regulate and therefore was constitutionally overbroad and violated defendants' right to free expression.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order.

State v. Adams


CA No. A68780


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


116 Ore. App. 156; 840 P.2d 745; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 2034


February 28, 1992, Argued and submitted  
November 4, 1992, Decided  
November 4, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Michael H. Marcus, Judge pro tempore. No. C9010-36005.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Oregon sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which sustained defendant's demurrers to his indictments for violating Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.270 by being a felony in possession of a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. 166.270 for three counts of being a felon in possession of a firearm. Defendant filed a demurrer, arguing that he was not felon because his prior second degree burglary conviction had been reduced to a misdemeanor after he completed probation. The trial court held that he had been a felon, but that Or. Rev. Stat. 166.270 violated the ex post facto clauses of the Or. Const. art. I, § 21 and U.S. Const. art. I, §9 because it retrospectively imposed additional penalties for the past felony. On appeal by the State, the court reversed. The court held that precedent established that § 166.270 was not unconstitutional. The court further held that even if defendant's conviction became a misdemeanor pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.585(2)(f) at the time he completed probation, it was still a felony at the time judgment was entered immediately following his guilty plea. Therefore, he was a felon for the purposes of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.270.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had sustained defendant's demurrers to his indictments for being a felon in possession of a firearm.

 

917 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fish


CA No. A67743


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


115 Ore. App. 609; 839 P.2d 278; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 1946


November 15, 1991, Argued and submitted  
October 21, 1992, Decided  
October 21, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 10, 1993. Petition for Review Pending 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Clackamas County. John K. Lowe, Judge. No. TC90-11996.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant motorist was charged with driving under the influence of intoxicants (DUII), ORS 813.010. The District Court of Clackamas County (Oregon) suppressed evidence of defendant's refusal to perform field sobriety tests. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: A deputy testified at the suppression hearing that he stopped defendant after observing his vehicle swerving. After approaching defendant, the deputy saw a can of beer on the floorboard, smelled alcohol, and saw that defendant's eyes were bloodshot and watery. The deputy testified that defendant refused to take field sobriety tests. Defendant moved to suppress evidence of his refusal to perform the tests. The trial court allowed the motion upon the ground that the deputy did not adequately advise defendant of his rights. The deputy told defendant that his refusal "could be used against him as evidence in court." The deputy did not employ the precise language of ORS 813.136. On appeal, the court held that the variation in the form or order of the deputy's advice was not fatal. The context of his advice would have led a reasonable person to understand that "in court" referred to a legal proceeding regarding the DUII. The court held that ORS 813.135 and ORS 813.136 extended the implied consent law to field sobriety tests. Thus, drivers consent to the tests and the State could present evidence of a motorist's refusal to perform those tests.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the suppression of the evidence and remanded for a trial.

Nelson v. Benton County


CA No. A75872


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


115 Ore. App. 453; 839 P.2d 233; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 1849


August 26, 1992, Argued and submitted  
October 14, 1992, Decided  
October 14, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Judicial Review from Land Use Board of Appeals. LUBA No. 92-035.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner farmer applied to build a nonfarm dwelling on his 1.37-acre parcel in an exclusive farm use zone. Defendant county denied the application and the Oregon Land Use Board of Appeals affirmed the ruling. The farmer appealed the board of appeals' judgment.


OVERVIEW: The farmer argued that the board of appeals erred by upholding the county's finding without requiring it to apply a "balancing test" to the evidence in arriving at the finding that the land was not unsuitable for agricultural production. The question before the county was not what weight the standard itself should be given, but what weight to give the evidence tending to show that the standard was or was not satisfied. The court held that the farmer's argument was self-defeating because the county necessarily and obviously did balance and weigh the evidence. The farmer's real complaint was that the way in which the county weighed the evidence did not balance in his favor. However, if there was substantial evidence in the whole record to substantiate the finding, neither the board of appeals nor the court could disturb it. The denial of the permit to build a nonfarm dwelling on the basis that the land had to be farmed and due to its size had to be farmed in combination with adjacent lands was not a taking of the farmer's property because it did not compel him to sell his land.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board of appeals' judgment.

 

919 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Eugene v. Kruk


CA No. A71272


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


115 Ore. App. 494; 839 P.2d 250; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 1858


May 11, 1992, Argued and submitted  
October 14, 1992, Decided  
October 14, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 16, 1992. Petition for Review Pending 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Lane County. Bryan T. Hodges, Judge. (Trial). Frank R. Alderson, Judge. (Demurrer). No. 91-50006.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the District Court, Lane County (Oregon), which convicted defendant under Eugene, Or., Municipal Code § 4.907 for interfering with a police officer. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in overruling her demurrer because the municipal ordinance under which she was convicted was preempted by state law.


OVERVIEW: While defendant's brother was being arrested, she yelled at one of the police officers and refused to stay back when ordered. Defendant also grabbed an officer's flashlight and prevented the officer from assisting with the arrest of defendant's brother. The court agreed with defendant that the municipal ordinance under which defendant was convicted was preempted by Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.315 because the ordinance prohibited conduct allowed by the statute. Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.315 criminalized physical force that created a substantial risk of physical injury. Eugene, Or., Municipal Code § 4.907, on the other hand, expressly criminalized any physical act, including a refusal to leave. The legislature had expressly excluded passive resistance from the scope of Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.315, but it was within the scope of Eugene, Or., Municipal Code § 4.907. The court denied the City's claim that Eugene, Or., Municipal Code § 4.910 was to be read in pari materia with Eugene, Or., Municipal Code § 4.907 to require proof of violence, physical force or any other means that created a substantial risk of physical injury to any person.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment convicting defendant of interfering with a police officer.

State v. Coven


CA No. A68722


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


115 Ore. App. 538; 839 P.2d 261; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 1861



October 14, 1992, Decided  
October 14, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Submitted on respondent's motion for reconsideration filed May 27, reconsideration allowed; opinion (112 Or App 657, 828 P2d 1063); Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Jack L. Mattison, Judge. No. 10-90-05327A.



DISPOSITION: Reconsideration allowed; opinion modified by affirming conviction for endangering welfare of minor; remanded for resentencing on that change; opinion adhered to as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought reconsideration of the court's decision ordering the circuit court to dismiss the indictment against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in a three-count indictment with unlawful delivery of a controlled substance, unlawful possession of a controlled substance, and endangering the welfare of a minor, each drug count including an allegation that defendant committed the crime as part of a drug cultivation, manufacture, or delivery scheme or network. The circuit court overruled defendant's demurrer to the indictment, in which he argued that the scheme or network allegation was unconstitutionally vague, and convicted him on all charges. Agreeing with defendant's grounds for demurrer, the court held that the circuit court erred in overruling it, reversed the conviction, and remanded the case with instructions to dismiss the indictment. The state contended that even disregarding the "scheme or network" allegation, the indictment still charged controlled substance offenses, so the circuit court properly overruled the demurrer. Because the argument had then recently been decided adversely to the state's contention, the court rejected it.


OUTCOME: The court allowed reconsideration and modified its opinion by affirming the conviction for endangering the welfare of a minor and remanding the case for resentencing on that change.

 

921 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Carlson v. Valley Mechanical


CA No. A69753


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


115 Ore. App. 371; 838 P.2d 637; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 1778


April 20, 1992, Argued and submitted  
September 30, 1992, Decided  
September 30, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 16, 1992. Petition for Review Denied January 26, 1993 (315 Or 311).


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review from Workers' Compensation Board. No. 90-09177.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant sought review of the order of the Workers' Compensation Board (Oregon). The board adopted a referee's order and affirmed his decision denying workers' compensation aggravation benefits to the claimant which were made against respondent employer.


OVERVIEW: Shortly before the claimant's aggravation rights expired (nearly five years after his injury), his employer received chart notes from his chiropractor. The employer treated the notes as a claim for aggravation, which it denied. Then, in a hearing on the denial that was held shortly after the effective date of amendments to ORS 656.273(3), the referee, applying the amendments, affirmed the employer's denial. The board adopted the referee's order and affirmed the decision. The court affirmed. The court held that, per Oregon Laws 1990, chapter 2, § 54, the 1990 amendments applied to all claims existing or arising on or after the effective date, regardless of the date of injury. Further, because Oregon Laws 1990, chapter 2, § 54(2) saved some cases that were heard before the effective date from being heard by the amendments, the fact that this case was not heard before then made it subject to the amendments. The court also held that there was substantial evidence to support the board's finding that the claimant did not have a compensable aggravation. Finally, the court dispensed with the claimant's argument that retroactive application of the 1990 amendments was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board's decision.

 

922 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Hudson v. Feder


CA No. A67213


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


115 Ore. App. 1; 836 P.2d 779; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 1680


May 8, 1992, Argued and submitted  
August 26, 1992, Decided  
August 26, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 14, 1992. Petition for Review Denied November 24, 1992 (314 Or 727).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Josephine County. Joan G. Seitz, Judge. No. 90-CV-0139.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions to dismiss.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant initiative sponsor sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court, Josephine County (Oregon), which entered a judgment in favor of plaintiff county official declaring the sponsor's initiative invalid.


OVERVIEW: The county's voters approved the initiative measure that amended the county charter in a way that reduced the present salaries of the county commissioners. The county official, who had overall administrative responsibilities for the payment of salaries, filed the instant declaratory action against the initiative sponsor seeking to have the initiative declared invalid. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the county official, and declared the initiative invalid. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court, and remanded the matter with instructions to dismiss the action. The court held that the action was not justiciable. The voters had already passed the initiative, and the sponsor had no more authority over and responsibility for the initiative after its passage. No relief could have been directed at the sponsor that would have rendered the cause justiciable. There was no defendant in the county official's case that would have made a meaningful judicial remedy possible. The action had to be dismissed because the absence of a justiciable controversy in the declaratory judgment action was a jurisdictional defect.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which entered a judgment in favor of the county official declaring the sponsor's initiative invalid. The court remanded the action with directions to order a dismissal.

 

923 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Sumner v. Choate


CA No. A69807


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


114 Ore. App. 406; 834 P.2d 535; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 1482


February 3, 1992, Argued and submitted  
July 22, 1992, Decided  
July 22, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Tillamook County. Delbert D. Mayer, Judge. No. 91-2002.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a petition for post-conviction relief nearly eight months after his guilty plea to a charge of delivery of a controlled substance became final. The Circuit Court, Tillamook County (Oregon) dismissed his petition for post-conviction relief on the ground that his claim was barred by the statute of limitations, Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.510(2)(a). Petitioner sought review.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from the dismissal of his petition for post-conviction relief, petitioner raised constitutional challenges to the 120-day limitation period that applied to the filing of a petition for post-conviction relief under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.510(2)(a). He also argued that he raised issues that he could not reasonably have raised within 120 days after his conviction became final. Affirming the dismissal, the court declined to address petitioner's challenges to the limitation period because he raised them for the first time on appeal. The court also did not find that his petition alleged facts that, if supported by evidence, were going to establish that the grounds for relief could not reasonably have been raised timely. Petitioner alleged that his trial attorney was ineffective, because he did not file a demurrer challenging the constitutionality of the "scheme or network" language in the charging instrument. The record showed that petitioner had already contemplated the constitutional infirmity of the "scheme or network" language in the guidelines. He did not explain why he could not reasonably have asserted his vagueness challenge in a timely fashion and in the correct forum.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court dismissing the petition for post-conviction relief.

 

924 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Graf


CA No. A69280


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


114 Ore. App. 275; 835 P.2d 934; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 1500


April 1, 1992, Argued and submitted  
July 22, 1992, Decided  
July 22, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 4, 1992. Petition for Review Denied November 24, 1992 (314 Or 727).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Union County. Ronald D. Schenck, Judge. Nos. 90-06-33472, 90-06-33473, 90-06-33474.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Union County (Oregon), which dismissed two indictments that had been filed against defendant for theft. Defendant, a Department of Transportation employee, claimed that the indictments should be dismissed under U.S. Const. amend. V and Or. Const. art. I, § 12, after he was forced to testify against himself during Department termination proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted, in three separate indictments. The Department thereafter notified him that it was commencing dismissal proceedings. Under Or. Admin. R. 105-80-003, defendant was entitled to an informal pretermination hearing and also a more formal, post-termination appeal. Although he was not required to appear at the pretermination hearing, Rule 105-80-003(6)(d) precluded defendant from refuting or offering evidence in mitigation at the later hearing if he did not appear at the earlier one. Defendant appeared and testified at the pretermination hearing. He then successfully filed a motion in the trial court to dismiss two of the indictments on that ground that his testimony was compelled within the meaning of the Fifth Amendment and Or. Const. art. I, § 12. He claimed, therefore, that he had transactional immunity. In reversing, the court held that the Department's procedures compelled defendant to testify against himself in violation of his constitutional rights. The Oregon Constitution, however, did not automatically grant transactional immunity for violations of the right against self-incrimination. Defendant's remedy was to file a suppression motion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that dismissed the indictments and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

925 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Gilliam County v. Department of Envtl. Quality


CA Nos. A68441 (Control), A68455 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


114 Ore. App. 369; 837 P.2d 965; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 1476


September 6, 1991, Argued and submitted  
July 22, 1992, Decided  
July 22, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Gilliam County's Petition for Reconsideration and Columbia Resource Company's Petition for Reconsideration Denied November 4, 1992. Both Petitions for Review Allowed December 22, 1992 (315 Or 271).


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review of Administrative Rules.



DISPOSITION: Rules held valid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a county and two solid waste disposal facilities, challenged the constitutionality of two rules of respondent Department of Environmental Quality (DEQ) that were adopted by respondent Environmental Quality Commission (EQC).


OVERVIEW: The part of the rules that petitioners challenged imposed a surcharge for in-state disposal of garbage generated out-of-state. Petitioners conceded that the DEQ had the general authority to make the rules. Petitioners' procedural argument was that Or. Rev. Stat. § 459.298 required the DEQ to follow a process that violated the Oregon Constitution and that the statute in its entirety was therefore invalid, so no rules could have been made under it. Petitioners argued in the alternative that if the procedures were permissible then the rules were invalid because the DEQ had not followed those procedures. Petitioner further argued that if the rules were made by a valid procedure, they were nonetheless invalid because they impermissibly discriminated against interstate commerce in violation of the United States Constitution. The court held that the rules were valid because before the court could have said that the rules were unconstitutional, petitioners would have had to show that the fees were excessive for the purposes for which they were collected or that there was no sufficient relation between the measure employed and the extent or manner of use of the state provided service.


OUTCOME: The court held that the rules adopted by the EQC that imposed a surcharge for in-state disposal of garbage generated out-of-state were valid.

State v. Rice


CA Nos. A65744 (Control), A65745, A65746, A65747 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


114 Ore. App. 101; 836 P.2d 731; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 1386


August 30, 1991, Argued and submitted; April 15, 1992, Taken In Banc and resubmitted  
July 8, 1992, Decided  
July 8, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied September 16, 1992. Petition for Review Denied October 27, 1992 (314 Or 574).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Lane County. Winfred K. Liepe, Judge. Nos. 90-20074, 90-20111, 90-20112, 90-20137.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the District Court, Lane County (Oregon), which convicted him on his plea to seven counts of negotiating bad checks and sentenced him to 90 days in the county jail for each conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to seven counts of negotiating a bad check, a Class A misdemeanor. Defendant was sentenced to 90 days in the county jail on each conviction with the sentences to be served consecutively. On review, defendant argued that his sentence exceeded the maximum authorized by law. The court found that the trial court had wide discretion in sentencing a misdemeanor offense. Furthermore, defendant's history showed a pattern of check-related offenses in which he used aliases, invalid addresses, different Social Security numbers, and different dates of birth. The court concluded that the trial court's 90-day sentence was well within the maximum authorized by Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.545 and that it was not so disproportionate to the offense as to shock the conscience of fair-minded individuals. Therefore, the trial court's decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision that sentenced defendant to 90 days in the county jail for each of his seven convictions of writing bad checks was affirmed.

 

927 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Fine v. Zenon


CA No. A70371


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


114 Ore. App. 183; 834 P.2d 509; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 1422


December 19, 1991, Submitted on record and briefs  
July 8, 1992, Decided  
July 8, 1992, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Richard D. Barber, Judge. No. 91C-10112.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon) that dismissed his untimely petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner's application for post-conviction relief was not timely filed. Because petitioner was not allowed a hearing under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.510(2), the issue was whether his petition alleged facts that, if supported by evidence, would have established that the grounds for relief could not reasonably have been raised timely. The court reversed the dismissal of petitioner's application, concluding that a timely petition was not prerequisite to the filing of an untimely petition that raised meritorious issues that could not reasonably have been raised within the 120-day limitation period and that the post-conviction court erred by dismissing the petition without a hearing. The limitation period began to run when the court granted petitioner's motion to dismiss his appeal. Petitioner was not on constructive notice that the court had granted his motion until his attorney informed him more than 120 days later, and he filed his petition within a week after that date. If the allegations in his petition were true, he could not reasonably have raised any grounds for relief within the limitations period.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

928 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anderson


CA No. A67101


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


113 Ore. App. 416; 833 P.2d 321; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 1125


May 15, 1991, Argued and submitted; June 3, 1992, Taken in banc and resubmitted  
June 10, 1992  
June 10, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Multnomah County. Ronald Cinniger, Judge pro tempore. No. P196211.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed; order of restitution vacated; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to DUII, Or. Rev. Stat. § 813.010. The District Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), suspended imposition of sentence and placed him on probation. One of the conditions of probation required him to pay $ 200 in restitution. Defendant objected on the ground that there was no evidence in the record to support that or any other figure. The trial court entered a sentencing order, including restitution of $ 200. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Because defendant pled guilty, his appeal was governed by Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 138.050 and 138.053, which limited the court's review to whether the disposition exceeded the maximum allowable by law or was unconstitutionally cruel and unusual. The question before the court was: What was a disposition that "exceeded the maximum allowable by law"? The court held that disposition was legally defective and, therefore, exceeded the maximum allowable by law if it was not imposed consistently with the statutory requirements. The court overruled State v. Peters, 104 Or. App. 582, 801 P.2d 904 (1990); State v. King, 107 Or. App. 249, 810 P.2d 413 (1991); and State v. Ross, 108 Or. App. 560, 815 P.2d 719 (1991). The court noted that the record revealed that the State failed to investigate and present to the trial court, prior to or at the time of sentencing, evidence of the nature and amount of damages, Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.106(1). The burden was on the State to prove the amount of restitution, and it failed to do that. With that, and because defendant objected to the sufficiency of the evidence but was not afforded a hearing, the restitution order exceeded the maximum allowable by law.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed, the order of restitution was vacated, and the case was remanded for resentencing.

 

929 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stevens


CA No. A66794


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


113 Ore. App. 429; 833 P.2d 318; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 1133


February 3, 1992, Argued and submitted  
June 10, 1992  
June 10, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Washington County. Gregory Milnes, Judge. No. D901370M.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court, Washington County (Oregon), which convicted defendant of carrying a concealed weapon violating Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.240 and denied defendant's motion for acquittal on the grounds that § 166.240 was applicable to a person who carried a concealed switchblade within the confines of his own home and § 166.240 did not violate Or. Const. art. I, § 27.


OVERVIEW: Officers went to defendant's residence to execute an arrest warrant. Defendant's wife consented to a search and defendant was found hiding. Before placing defendant into the police car he was frisked and a switchblade was found in his pocket. At trial, an officer testified that the arrest was predicated on defendant's having carried a switchblade in his pocket both inside and outside the house. On review, the court held that a switchblade was the type of weapon that came within the meaning of "arms" in Or. Const. art. I, § 27, and accordingly, the "mere possession or carrying of" a switchblade could not be absolutely proscribed by the legislature. Possession of a billy club inside one's home was protected by the constitutional right to bear arms in defense of one's person and property. "Mere possession" even outside the home was protected. Or. Const. art. I, § 27 was not qualified as to place. Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.240 was applied unconstitutionally. The concealing within one's own home was not the type of unrestrained rights-exercising that posed a clear threat to public safety. Section 166.240 applied only to the carrying of concealed weapons outside one's own home.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court, which convicted defendant of carrying a concealed weapon. The trial court erred in denying defendant's motion for acquittal.

Hass v. Port of Portland


CA A65836


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


112 Ore. App. 308; 829 P.2d 1008; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 711


September 23, 1991, Argued and submitted  
April 8, 1992, Decided  
April 8, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 1, 1992. Petition for Review Denied September 29, 1992 (314 Or 391).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. William J. Keys, Judge pro tempore. No. A8909-05117.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which directed a verdict against him on one of his claims and entered judgment reflecting a jury verdict in favor of defendant Port of Portland (airport) on all other claims in the citizen's action against the airport for damages for assault and battery, false arrest, false imprisonment, and wrongful initiation of a civil proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The citizen left his vehicle unattended at the curbside pickup area of an airport terminal. The airport police officer and the citizen argued and finally were involved in an altercation. The police office gave the citizen a ticket and the citizen instituted an action against the airport. The trial court directed a verdict against the citizen on one of the claims and the jury found in favor of the airport on the other claims. The citizen appealed. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded. The court found that the trial court erred by admitting the statements made by the judge in the citizen's infraction hearing, which was held for the purpose of adjudicating the citizen's ticket. The court found that Or. Rev. Stat. § 153.260 precluded evidence of any plea, finding or proceeding from an infraction proceeding. Therefore, the trial court erred in admitting the evidence and the case was reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which found in favor of the airport and remanded the citizen's case against the airport for damages for assault and battery, false arrest, false imprisonment, and wrongful initiation of a civil proceeding.

Moser v. Frohnmayer


CA A67796


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


112 Ore. App. 226; 829 P.2d 84; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 590


January 29, 1992, Argued and submitted  
April 1, 1992, Decided  
April 1, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 1, 1992. Petition for Review Allowed September 29, 1992 (314 Or 391).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Richard D. Barber, Judge. No. 89C-12416.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff businessman appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), in favor of defendant State in the businessman's declaratory judgment action that challenged the constitutionality of Or. Rev. Stat. § 759.290.


OVERVIEW: The businessman brought a declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of Or. Rev. Stat. § 759.290, which prohibited the use of automatic dialing and announcing devices to solicit the purchase of any realty, goods or services. The trial court ruled in favor of the State. On appeal, the court reversed and found the statute unconstitutional. There was no basis under the Oregon Constitution to provide more protection to certain nonabusive communication based upon the content of the communication. It did not give different subjects of speech different levels of protection. Because § 759.290 regulated commercial speech differently from other subjects of speech, it was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the State in the businessman's declaratory judgment action.

State v. Guthrie


CA A67307 (Control) & CA A67334


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


112 Ore. App. 102; 828 P.2d 462; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 506


August 30, 1991, Argued and submitted  
March 11, 1992, Decided  
March 11, 1992, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Jackson County. Mitchell A. Karaman, Judge. No. 90-1173-C-3.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Circuit Court, Jackson County (Oregon) for assault in the first degree, Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.185. Defendant also challenged the upward departure sentence imposed on the assault conviction and his conviction for attempted murder, Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.115.


OVERVIEW: The victim testified that he saw defendant and his brother beating up a third man. He tried to pull defendant away and was stabbed. Under the sentencing guidelines, assault in the first degree was in crime seriousness category 10 if the victim did not substantially contribute to the commission of the offense by precipitating the attack. Or. Admin. R. 253-04-002. According to defendant, the phrase "precipitating the attack" was unconstitutionally vague on its face. The court, however, ruled that the language of the subcategory provided adequate notice to a person that an unprovoked assault was a more serious offense. Defendant also argued that the sentencing court erred in imposing an upward departure sentence of 180 months. The State conceded that the sentencing court erred in relying on three aggravating factors: violence toward the victim, use of a weapon, and permanent injury to the victim. The court remanded, but held that the sentencing court could properly consider both persistent involvement in similar offenses and prison discipline problems, as aggravating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and remanded for resentencing.

State v. Renly


CA A66432


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


111 Ore. App. 453; 827 P.2d 1345; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 466


July 22, 1991, Argued and submitted  
February 26, 1992, Decided  
February 26, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Linn County. William O. Lewis, Judge. No. 89082160.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court, Linn County (Oregon), which convicted defendant of sexual abuse in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction, and on appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that a witness's testimony about the children's statements was not independently admissible under Or. R. Evid. 803(18a)(b) because (1) the state did not provide the requisite notice that it intended to introduce that hearsay at trial and (2) the trial court did not make the requisite findings that the declarants were unavailable, the statements were inherently reliable and other evidence corroborated the acts and defendant's participation in them. The court held that that it did not in any way tend to negate explain or counterbalance any misleading or unfair impression that defendant's evidence could possibly have caused the jury and there was no "open door" to its admissibility. The court noted that because testimony concerning the sexual misconduct was not presented in the pretrial hearing, where corroborative evidence should have been presented before the hearsay can be found admissible, the court could not rule on it now.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of sexual abuse in the first degree and remanded for a new trial.

 

934 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stevens


CA A67304


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


111 Ore. App. 258; 826 P.2d 12; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 334


June 21, 1991, Argued and submitted  
February 12, 1992, Decided  
February 12, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Polk County. Charles E. Luukinen, Judge. No. 90P-3215.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by the Circuit Court, Polk County (Oregon) convicting and sentencing him to two counts of drug-related felonies. Defendant had pled guilty to the charges.


OVERVIEW: Several counts in the indictment alleged that defendant's conduct was part of a drug manufacture scheme. Defendant demurred to the counts, arguing that the "scheme or network" allegations were unconstitutionally vague. The trial court overruled the demurrer, and defendant pled guilty. He did not dispute the grid block or the presumptive sentence of 16 to 18 months. The trial court imposed a 16-month prison term. After defendant's sentence, the Oregon Court of Appeals held that the "scheme or network" language violated Article I, sections 20 and 21, of the Oregon Constitution. On appeal, defendant attacked the overruling of his demurrer and the imposition of sentence. Affirming, the court held that it had no authority to review the trial court's ruling on the demurrer because defendant had pled guilty. Although ORS 138.222(4)(b) allowed review of the classification of the crime seriousness on a sentencing appeal, ORS 138.222(2)(d) precluded review of a sentence imposed under a plea agreement. In addition, defendant's claim was not reviewable under ORS 138.222(4)(b), nor was it reviewable under ORS 138.222(4)(a) as a failure by the sentencing court to follow the requirements of law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Davenport v. Gruber


CA A61071


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


111 Ore. App. 280; 826 P.2d 59; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 343


December 14, 1990, Argued and submitted; September 18, 1991, Resubmitted In Banc  
February 12, 1992, Decided  
February 12, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Lincoln County. Robert J. Huckleberry, Judge. No. 88-3702.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant purchasers appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Lincoln County (Oregon), which granted summary judgment to plaintiffs, record owners of the property, and denied the purchasers' motion for summary judgment in the record owners' action to quiet title to standing timber.


OVERVIEW: The record owners obtained an assignment from the timber rights owner of his interest prior to the natural expiration of that interest, but did not record the assignment. However, the deed records showed that they owned the property and the timber rights by virtue of the eventual reversion of the timber rights. The timber rights owner had failed to pay property taxes assessed against the timber interest, and the county foreclosed its tax lien on the timber. Even though the record owners owned both the land and the timber by that time, they were not named as parties or given notice of the foreclosure, and the county obtained a tax deed. They then sold a portion of the land to the purchasers, who discovered the county's deed to the timber and purchased the interest, later announcing a plan to log the timber. The record owners filed the instant action and the purchasers counterclaimed to quiet title. The trial court granted the record owners' motion for summary judgment, and the purchasers appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the record owners' interest was a matter of public record and the foreclosure without notice deprived them of their property without due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting summary judgment to the record owners in their action against the purchasers to quiet title to timber rights.

State v. Long


CA A65593


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


110 Ore. App. 599; 823 P.2d 1031; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 135



January 15, 1992, Decided  
January 15, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 19, 1992. Petition for Review Allowed April 28, 1992 (313 Or 209).


PRIOR HISTORY: On appellant's petition for reconsideration filed November 12, 1991, petition for reconsideration allowed; decision (109 Or App 221, 818 P2d 996); Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Pierre L. Van Rysselberghe, Judge. No. 10-90-00555.



DISPOSITION: Petition for reconsideration allowed; decision adhered to.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned for review of a decision affirming, without opinion, his conviction for supplying contraband, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.185.


OVERVIEW: The jail promulgated and implemented a rule that defined "contraband" to include tobacco, matches, and rolling papers. Defendant was accused of possessing these items. He demurred to the indictment, arguing that § 162.185 unconstitutionally delegated authority to local governments to define "contraband." The trial court denied the demurrer, and defendant was convicted. He appealed his conviction, which was affirmed without opinion. Defendant petitioned for reconsideration. The court allowed the petition and adhered to its decision. The court held that the Oregon Constitution did not prohibit the delegation of legislative authority, if a statutory scheme contained standards that circumscribed an agency's exercise of delegated powers. The legislature defined "contraband" in Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.135(1). The court found that the definition was a constitutionally sufficient directive to state and local agencies that were given the power to issue rules and orders defining contraband.


OUTCOME: The court allowed the petition for reconsideration and adhered to its decision affirming defendant's conviction for supplying contraband.

Bartz v. State


CA A67398


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


110 Ore. App. 614; 825 P.2d 657; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 136


July 26, 1991, Argued and submitted  
January 15, 1992, Decided  
January 15, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 19, 1992. Petition for Review Allowed April 24, 1992 (313 Or 209).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Deschutes County. Thomas M. Mosgrove, Judge. No. 90-CV-0091-TM.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Deschutes County (Oregon), which granted respondent State's motion to dismiss his petition for post-conviction relief on the ground that it was barred by the statute of limitations in Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.510.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner was convicted of rape in the third degree. More than 120 days later, he filed a petition for post-conviction relief, claiming that he was denied his rights to due process and effective assistance of counsel because his attorney did not inform him of a potential statutory defense to the rape charge. The trial court dismissed the petition on the ground that it was barred by the 120-day statute of limitations in § 138.510. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order. The court held that the petitioner had the sole responsibility of investigating the grounds for a collateral attack on his conviction, so his attorney's omission did not excuse the late filing of the petition. The court determined that the 120-day statute of limitations in § 138.510 did not violate defendant's right to due process or impermissibly suspend the writ of habeas corpus in violation of Or. Const. art. I, § 23. The court ruled that states were permitted to impose reasonable time limitations on the assertion of federal rights, and that the Oregon Constitution did not prohibit reasonable time limitations on the availability of post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the petitioner's petition for post-conviction relief.

In re Marriage of Thompson and Thompson


CA A70287


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


110 Ore. App. 462; 823 P.2d 1001; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 35


November 22, 1991, Argued and submitted  
January 8, 1992, Decided  
January 8, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 4, 1992. Petition for Review Denied March 24, 1992 (313 Or 75).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Maurice K. Merten, Judge. No. 15-87-01072.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded. No costs to either party.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of an order of the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which dismissed her motion to modify respondent father's child support obligation pursuant to former ORS 25.285.


OVERVIEW: The judgment of dissolution ordered the father to pay child support through the Department of Human Resources. The father moved to dismiss the mother's motion to modify his support obligations on the ground that it did not allege a substantial change of circumstances, which he asserted was a prerequisite to modification under former ORS 25.285 (Oregon), as well as ORS 107.135. The father also argued that if such a showing was not required for parents whose support was payable through an enforcing agency as it was for all other parents, then former ORS 25.285 was unconstitutional in violation of his equal protection rights. On appeal, the court held that the classification created by former ORS 25.285 was created by the statute itself rather than by virtue of the characteristics of the class, therefore, the statute was not unconstitutional. Under ORS 25.285, the class defined by parents whose support was payable through an enforcing agency was simply a natural result of law-making. Such a classification did not violate the Oregon Constitution. Because the statute was not unconstitutional, the circuit court erred by dismissing the mother's motion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's order and remanded the case. The court ruled that no costs were to be awarded to either party.

State v. Rodriguez


CA A62825


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


110 Ore. App. 544; 823 P.2d 1026; 1992 Ore. App. LEXIS 47


February 27, 1991, Argued and submitted  
January 8, 1992, Decided  
January 8, 1992, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Thomas L. Moultrie, Judge pro tempore. No. C89-01-30382.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which convicted him on two counts of being an ex-convict in possession of a firearm in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.270.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was subject to deportation because he was an alien who had been convicted of possession of drugs. A federal agent obtained an administrative warrant for defendant's arrest. Defendant allowed the agent and others with the agent to enter his home and consented to a search, where they found pistols. Defendant contended that the arrest warrant was invalid under the Fourth Amendment and Or. Const. art. I, § 9 because it was unsupported by affirmation, and he sought to have the pistol suppressed. The State argued that the warrant did not require an affirmation. On appeal, the court reversed the decision, finding that for state prosecutions in state court, an arrest warrant was invalid if it was not supported by affirmation. The court rejected the State's contention that a certified copy of defendant's prior conviction satisfied the affirmation requirement. Further, the agent's sole purpose in bringing members of the regional narcotics task force with him was to have them look for evidence of violations of state narcotics law. The court found that the agent sought to utilize the administrative warrant for purposes beyond accomplishing defendant's deportation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of defendant's motion to suppress and remanded the cause for a new trial.
