State v. Hibbard


CA A66866


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


110 Ore. App. 335; 823 P.2d 989; 1991 Ore. App. LEXIS 1894


July 19, 1991, Argued and submitted  
December 18, 1991, Decided  
December 18, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 4, 1992. Petition for Review Denied April 28, 1992 (313 Or 211).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Clackamas County. Steven L. Maurer, Judge. No. 90-12365.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the District Court of Clackamas County (Oregon) for telephonic harassment in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. §166.090(1)(a), arguing that the trial court erred by denying his motions for directed verdict and for judgment of acquittal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction was based upon three telephone calls he made in a single day to a 9-1-1 operator. During the first call, defendant initially said, "Huh?" During the second call, he used profane language. In the last call, he requested police assistance because of an altercation involving guns and knives. When the police officers arrived at defendant's home and questioned defendant, he responded that he was "sitting here drinking whiskey and dialing 9-1-1 for entertainment." On appeal, defendant argued that his conduct did not violate Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.090(1)(a), because he communicated to the 9-1-1 operator after each call was answered. He also challenged the statute's constitutionality. Upholding the conviction, the court held that there was sufficient evidence to conclude that defendant had the requisite intent under § 166.090(1)(a); specifically, that he had no communicative purpose when he placed the calls. The statute did not violate the First Amendment or. Const. art. I, § 8 because it regulated the conduct of placing the calls and not the content of defendant's comments to the 9-1-1 operator. The statute was not overbroad or vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

944 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Spinney


CA No. A64690


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


109 Ore. App. 573; 820 P.2d 854; 1991 Ore. App. LEXIS 1678


August 30, 1991, Argued and submitted  
November 13, 1991, Decided  
November 13, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 26, 1991. Petition for Review Allowed January 21, 1992 (312 Or 588). Petition for Review Dismissed March 3, 1992 (313 Or 75).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Benton County. Robert S. Gardner, Judge. No. CM89-0966.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court, Benton County (Oregon), which convicted defendant of first degree burglary and second degree kidnapping. Defendant challenged the trial court's denial of his motion to hold the application of the Oregon Sentencing Guidelines unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court first denied defendant's claim that the Sentencing Guidelines violated Or. Const. art. I, § 15. The Guidelines' express acknowledgment that one of the primary purposes for imposing sentences was to provide punishment appropriate to an offense did not render them vindictive and violative of Or. Const. art. I, § 15. The Guidelines also met the proportionality requirement imposed by Or. Const. art. I, § 16 by reserving in incremental fashion progressively longer periods of incarceration for more serious crimes and the most recidivist offenders; criminal history and seriousness of the offense were factors necessary to be considered in imposing a sentence proportionate to the offense and offender. Finally, the court held that the Guidelines did not violate Or. Const. art. III, § 1, because a legislative determination that a certain sentence was required to be imposed did not violate the separation of powers requirement. The legislature's power to set criminal penalties did not impair the power of the judiciary to adjudicate, pronounce a judgment, or carry it into effect. Judges still had discretion to give weight to mitigating and aggravating factors of each case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting and sentencing defendant.

AFSCME Local 2623 v. Department of Corrections


CA No. A62602


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


109 Ore. App. 662; 820 P.2d 892; 1991 Ore. App. LEXIS 1684


June 25, 1991, Argued and submitted  
November 13, 1991, Decided  
November 13, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied January 15, 1992. Petition for Review Allowed February 25, 1992 (312 Or 676).


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review of Administrative Rules.



DISPOSITION: Rules held valid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employees sought judicial review of rules of respondent Oregon Department of Corrections that permitted warrantless searches of state corrections system employees.


OVERVIEW: The employees contended that the rules did not make it sufficiently clear that no criminal consequences would have attached to searches and seizures authorized by the rules. The Department argued that the searches were limited to persons employed in the operation of prisons. In that context, it contended that the authority to search was implicit in the statutory directives to Department to provide for the health and security of persons confined in state prisons. The court noted that not all agencies might have found implicit authority to search from a general legislative directive for the agency to provide for health and safety. However, given the serious risks posed by drugs or weapons in prison, the court concluded that the legislative directive to the Department to provide for safety carried with it the implicit authorization to intercept contraband and to do so, if necessary, by means of a search. The court held that the limits in the rules, including the requirement that searches be based on reasonable suspicion, sufficiently limited the Department's discretion and provided the measure of control over the search that would have been provided by a warrant.


OUTCOME: The court held that the Department's rules were valid.

State v. Warner

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Douglas County (Oregon) convicting him of criminal mistreatment in the first degree under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.205(1)(b). Defendant contended that § 163.205(1)(b) was void for vagueness.


OVERVIEW: The action arose out of the diagnosis of defendant's daughter with "shaken baby syndrome." Defendant contended that Or. Rev. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for criminal mistreatment in the first degree.

Salem Committee to Stop Food Irradiation v. Secretary of State


No. CA A61759


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


109 Ore. App. 364; 819 P.2d 752; 1991 Ore. App. LEXIS 1628


February 4, 1991, Argued and submitted  
October 30, 1991, Decided  
October 30, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 19, 1992. Petition for Review Denied April 28, 1992 (313 Or 210).


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review from Secretary of State.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner organizer of a committee to stop food irradiation sought review of an order of respondent Secretary of State (Oregon) that imposed a civil penalty against him under Or. Rev. Stat. § 260.118 for failure to timely file a contributions and expenditures statement after a failed initiative petition campaign.


OVERVIEW: The Secretary of State imposed a civil penalty against the organizer for failure to timely file a contributions and expenditures statement after a failed initiative petition campaign. The organizer sought review, alleging that Salem, Or., Rev. Code § 11.274(b), which limited to 100 days the period in which to circulate a particular petition for signatures, was unconstitutional. The court held that: (1) an ordinance violated Or. Const. art. IV, § 1 if it directly conflicted with that section or if it was an unreasonable regulation that unduly burdened the right of initiative; (2) Salem, Or., Rev. Code § 11.274(b) did not directly conflict with Or. Const. art. IV, § 1, which was silent as to any period for circulating petitions; (3) the ordinance did not unduly burden the organizer's initiative right; and (4) the Secretary did not err by imposing the penalty because the deadline that the city set for submitting signed petitions was not unconstitutional. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Secretary's imposition of a fine against the organizer for failure to timely file a contributions and expenditures statement after the failed initiative petition campaign.

Moore v. Motor Vehicles Div.


CA No. A65351


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


109 Ore. App. 195; 818 P.2d 974; 1991 Ore. App. LEXIS 1512


March 20, 1991, Argued and submitted  
October 9, 1991, Decided  
October 9, 1991, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review from Motor Vehicles Division. No. 08 890712 10045.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner driver sought judicial review of an order of the Motor Vehicles Division (MVD) (Oregon) that revoked his driving privileges when it affirmed the MVD's previous determination that the driver was a habitual traffic offender.


OVERVIEW: The driver was convicted of DUII, then DWS, and then another DUII. The MVD determined that the driver was a habitual traffic offender under ORS 809.600 and notified the driver of the revocation of his driving privileges. After a hearing, the hearing officer determined that the driver was a habitual traffic offender and ordered that his driving privileges be revoked. The driver challenged the MVD's use of the prior DUII and DWS convictions as underlying offenses in its determination. In affirming, the court held that ORS 809.640(5) & (6) simply provided the MVD with a method to verify that convictions shown in a driving record were actually entered against the designated person. They did not provide a method for testing the constitutionality of a prior conviction. There was nothing in ORS 809.640(5) that permitted a collateral attack on prior convictions in a habitual traffic offender proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the MVD's order.

State v. Burke


CA No. A63692


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


109 Ore. App. 7; 818 P.2d 511; 1991 Ore. App. LEXIS 1450


December 21, 1990, Argued and submitted; April 3, 1991, Taken In Banc and resubmitted  
September 25, 1991, Decided  
September 25, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 11, 1991. Petition for Review Denied January 28, 1992 (312 Or 589).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Jackson County. L. L. Sawyer, Judge. Nos. 86-1797-C-2, 86-1798-C-2.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order of the Circuit Court, Jackson County (Oregon) that set aside defendant's conviction for sexual abuse in the first degree, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.225.


OVERVIEW: The state challenged the trial court's set aside of defendant's prior conviction of sexual abuse in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.425, and asserted that Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.225 as amended in 1989 did not apply to defendant's conviction. The court reversed and found that the plain language of the amended version of § 137.225(5)(a)(D) explicitly provided that the statute did not apply to convictions of sexual abuse in the first degree under § 163.425. The court found that the key issue was whether the legislature intended the amended statute to apply to defendant's conviction that occurred prior to the enactment of the amended statute. Defendant asserted that application of the amended statute was a violation of the state and federal constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto legislation. The court noted that § 137.225(8) explicitly stated the legislature's intent that the amended statute apply to convictions that occurred prior to the statute's enactment. The court also held that the elimination of the set aside remedy for sexual abuse was not an ex post facto punishment because it did not increase his punishment, forestall parole, or extend his probation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed because the legislature intended retroactive application of the amended statute, and because the application of the amended statute to defendant's convictions was not contrary to the constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto legislation.

951 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Gruetzke v. Gresham


CA No. A64441


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


108 Ore. App. 325; 815 P.2d 228; 1991 Ore. App. LEXIS 1181


February 8, 1991, Argued and submitted  
July 31, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Marshall Amiton, Judge pro tempore. No. A8904-02127.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions to dismiss petition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and its manager, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which denied defendants' motion to dismiss plaintiff former police officer's petition for a writ of review of the city's decision to terminate the officer's employment.


OVERVIEW: The petition merely alleged that plaintiff was a police officer who could not be terminated without just cause and that he was terminated. The court held that it was insufficient because it only generally told the circuit court of the issues involved. Although the court could infer from the recitation in the petition that the officer was complaining that he had been terminated without just cause, the petition did not inform the court of the evidence to be addressed or provide sufficient facts to allow a determination of whether a writ should be issued ex parte. The officer alleged that defendants made a finding or order not supported by substantial evidence in the whole record, but the petition was silent as to what findings were being attacked. He alleged that defendants "improperly construed the applicable law," but the petition did not reveal what was improperly construed or what legal standard should have been used. Because the trial court had no way to determine whether defendants had exercised their functions erroneously, and defendants had no way to respond to the petition, the trial court should have granted defendants' motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the case with directions to grant the motion to dismiss the petition.

State ex rel Mikkelsen v. Hill


CA No. A66027


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


108 Ore. App. 135; 813 P.2d 1130; 1991 Ore. App. LEXIS 1069


May 15, 1991, Argued and submitted  
July 3, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Harney County. F. J. Yraguen, Judge. No. 89-11-9705-E.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Harney County (Oregon), which found him to be in criminal contempt for failure to pay child support.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was divorced and ordered to pay child support but he made no payments. A citation was issued for defendant to show cause why he should not be held in contempt. The trial court treated the matter as a criminal contempt. Although neither defendant nor the State called witnesses or presented evidence, the trial court found that defendant had "purposely and willfully failed" to comply with the support order and imposed a suspended sentence and a year of probation. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court shifted the burden of proof from the State to him in violation of the Due Process Clause. The court agreed, holding that the trial court impermissibly shifted the burden of proving defendant's ability or inability to pay from the State to defendant. Moreover, the State's evidence was insufficient to establish a prima facie case of contempt, including the ability to pay element, because there was no evidence to support a finding that defendant's failure to pay child support was "willful." Because the facts did not show that defendant was capable of complying with the support order, there was insufficient evidence of willfulness to find him guilty of criminal contempt.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

953 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Oberg v. Honda Motor Co.


CA No. A61587


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


108 Ore. App. 43; 814 P.2d 517; 1991 Ore. App. LEXIS 1040


April 22, 1991, Argued and submitted  
June 26, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Robert P. Jones, Judge. No. A8709-05897.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff victim filed an action against defendant manufacturer for product liability after the three-wheeled all-terrain vehicle the victim was driving flipped over. Pursuant to a jury verdict, the Circuit Court of Multnomah County (Oregon) entered a judgment in favor of the victim in the amount of $ 5,735,512.31. The manufacturer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court found that evidence of excerpts from several internal staff memoranda and an Advanced Notice of Proposed Rulemaking of the Consumer Product Safety Commission regarding all-terrain vehicles was properly admitted. It was admitted not to prove that the vehicle was defective, but for the limited purpose of showing the manufacturer's knowledge of the purportedly harmful characteristics of its product. The court also found that the punitive damages award did not violate Or. Const. art. I, § 16 because the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment did not apply in civil actions between private parties. Regarding the punitive damages award, the jury's discretion was exercised within reasonable constraints and the trial court's restrictive instructions adequately guided the jury during its consideration of the manufacturer's liability. Accordingly, the award of punitive damages did not violate due process. Finally, the manufacturer's motion for a new trial was properly denied because the newly discovered evidence probably would not have changed the result. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the victim was affirmed.

 

954 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hendrix


CA No. A65065


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


107 Ore. App. 734; 813 P.2d 1115; 1991 Ore. App. LEXIS 1014


February 1, 1991, Argued and submitted  
June 19, 1991, Decided  
June 19, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 2, 1991. Petition for Review Allowed November 26, 1991 (312 Or 525).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. James R. Ellis, Judge. No. C89-12-36913.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which convicted him of intimidation in the first degree in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.165(1)(a)(A).


OVERVIEW: Defendant and three cohorts encountered two Mexican men at a store. Without provocation, one of the cohorts began hitting the victims, and the others, including defendant, joined in the attacks. Witnesses heard the attackers yelling "white power" and taunting the victims to speak English. Defendant and one co-defendant were convicted by at bench trial; the other two cohorts were found guilty by a jury. On appeal, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant because although he claimed he did not shout any racial epithet, the trial court could infer unlawful motive by his conduct, which included his continued participation in the beating after his cohorts began yelling. The court rejected defendant's constitutional attacks, holding that the Intimidation Law: (1) was directed at conduct rather than speech; (2) was not vague based on its perception element, which focused on the actor's motivation rather than the victim's status; and (3) satisfied due process by providing notice of the prohibited conduct. Finding no error, the court affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment by the trial court, which convicted defendant of violating the Intimidation Law.

956 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sullens


CA No. A62348


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


106 Ore. App. 590; 809 P.2d 700; 1991 Ore. App. LEXIS 577


October 31, 1990, Argued and submitted  
April 17, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 24, 1991. Petition for Review Allowed August 20, 1991 (312 Or 80).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Deschutes County. Thomas M. Mosgrove, Judge. No. 89-CR-0005-TM.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Deschutes County (Oregon), convicted defendant of burglary in the first degree and theft in the first degree in violation of ORS 164.225 and ORS 164.055 (Oregon), respectively. He appealed, seeking review of the circuit court's order denying his motion for a new trial, which he filed on the ground of newly discovered evidence. The appeal raised a question of whether the order was appealable under ORS 138.040 (Oregon).


OVERVIEW: The State argued that there was no authority to review the denial of defendant motion for a new trial because the order denying it was filed after judgment was entered. The court agreed, even though ORS 138.040 gave defendant a right to appeal from a judgment or order that was described in ORS 138.053 (Oregon). There was nothing in ORS 138.040, the court ruled, authorizing a review of the post-judgment order denying defendant's motion. The court also noted that a post-judgment order was not an intermediate order, that ORS 136.535(1) (Oregon) allowed a motion for a new trial to be filed after judgment, and that ORS 138.071(2) delayed a judgment's effective date for purposes of appeal while a motion for new trial was pending. Those statutes, however, did not expressly or by implication authorize review of a post-judgment order denying a motion for a new trial. In addition, the court determined that ORS 138.053 specifically limited the type of post-judgment orders that could be appealed, which were subject to the limitations on review in ORS 138.040(1). The court also pointed out that appeals were allowed only when provided by statute and that the statutes had to be strictly applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

957 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Racicot


CA No. A61461


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


106 Ore. App. 557; 809 P.2d 726; 1991 Ore. App. LEXIS 548


August 24, 1990, Argued and submitted; December 12, 1990, resubmitted In Banc  
April 10, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. George J. Woodrich, Judge. No. 10-89-02459.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed; consecutive sentences vacated; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged consecutive sentences imposed by the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon) following his conviction on seven counts of an indictment. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in imposing consecutive sentences, because it failed to make findings justifying the sentences as required by Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.123(4).


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted on seven counts of an indictment, the trial court imposed consecutive sentences. Defendant appealed the sentences, arguing that the trial court had not made findings justifying the sentences as required by § 137.123(4). The court held that: 1) although the trial court was not required to state its reasons for imposing the consecutive sentences, or make special findings on the record, § 137.123(4) required the trial court to determine whether consecutive sentences were authorized by the statute; 2) there was no indication in the trial court's ruling imposing the consecutive sentences that the trial court made the finding that the consecutive sentences were authorized; therefore, 3) because the court's review was not de novo, and the trial court had not imposed the sentences in accordance with § 137.123(4), the sentences were vacated, and the matter remanded for resentencing after a determination by the trial court of whether the consecutive sentences were authorized by the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court entered on defendant's convictions; however, the court vacated the consecutive sentences imposed on the convictions and remanded the cause for resentencing.

 

958 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vaughn


CA No. A61085


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


105 Ore. App. 518; 805 P.2d 733; 1991 Ore. App. LEXIS 173


December 21, 1990, Argued and submitted  
February 6, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. George J. Woodrich, Judge. No. 10-78-8808.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Lane County (Oregon), continuing defendant's probation under Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.550(1)(a) and imposing additional conditions. The State had obtained a conviction and sentence against defendant for felony driving while his license was suspended in 1979.


OVERVIEW: The execution of defendant's sentence was suspended, and he was placed on probation for felony driving while his license was suspended for a period of three years. The trial court issued a bench warrant for defendant's arrest in 1980. Defendant was arraigned on the probation violation in 1989. The trial court entered an order that continued defendant's probation under Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.550(1)(a) and imposed additional conditions. Defendant argued that the trial court lacked jurisdiction because a valid arrest warrant had not been issued within the period of probation. The court affirmed because the bench warrant that was issued for defendant's arrest complied with the requirements of Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.060 and, therefore, the trial court retained jurisdiction to hold a hearing in 1989. When read with Or. Rev. Stat. § 131.005(2) and when compared with § 131.005(14), it was apparent that the legislature contemplated the issuance of a bench warrant to procure the appearance of a probationer who had absconded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that continued defendant's probation after the State obtained a conviction against him for felony driving while suspended.

 

959 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Moeller


CA No. A65221 (Control), CA Nos. A65222, A65223, A65224, A65225, A65226 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


105 Ore. App. 434; 806 P.2d 130; 1991 Ore. App. LEXIS 175


January 15, 1991, Argued and submitted  
February 6, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 3, 1991. Petition for Review Allowed May 7, 1991 (311 Or 349).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Clatsop County. William L. Jackson, Senior Judge. Nos. 89-1379, 89-1380, 89-1410, 89-1411, 89-1422, 89-1423.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, the State contested the orders by which the Circuit Court of Clatsop County (Oregon) sustained defendants' demurrers to their indictments for drug-related offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that the sentence enhancement provisions of Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.120(2), pertaining to crimes occurring as part of a drug cultivation, manufacture or delivery scheme or network, were unconstitutional. When defendants' motions carried before the trial court, the prosecution appealed to no avail. Defendants properly used demurrers to challenge the validity of penalty provisions that they contested. Facts constituting the crime were for the jury's resolution, while facts characterizing defendant were for the sentencing judge. Similarly, facts going to the criminal acts for which defendants would be punished had to be proved to the jury's satisfaction. Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.120(2) identified an issue to be decided by the trier of fact. The statute violated Or. Const. art. I, §§ 20, 21 because it was so uncertain or unclear that judges and juries had unbridled discretion to decide what conduct came within it, and it did not provide notice of the forbidden conduct. Under this second criterion, the statute was void because it was susceptible of an abundance of possible meanings and applications, all or none of which might be the intended ones.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders.

 

960 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Kilpatrick v. Snow Mountain Pine Co.


CA No. A62473


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


105 Ore. App. 240; 805 P.2d 137; 1991 Ore. App. LEXIS 115


July 16, 1990, Argued and submitted  
January 23, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 24, 1991. Petition for Review Denied May 28, 1991 (311 Or 426).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Grant County. R. T. Gooding, Judge. No. 89-04-0128 CV.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, successors to a landowner who deeded property to a railroad, sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court, Grant County (Oregon), which entered judgment in favor of defendants, successors to the railroad, in the landowner's successors' suit for trespass and conversion concerning the deeded land.


OVERVIEW: A landowner deeded land to a railroad for a right-of-way. The deed provided that if the land was abandoned or was no longer used as a railroad, the rights of the grantee would be deemed terminated and would revert to the grantor. The landowner's successor did not record its interest in the railroad strip by a deadline established by Or. Rev. Stat. § 105.772 for such recordation. Later, the railroad line was abandoned. The landowner's successors sued the railroad's successors for trespass and conversion. The trial court entered judgment for the railroad's successors. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that § 105.772 was not an ex post facto law in violation of U.S. Const. at. I, § 9 or Or. Const. art. I, § 21 because only criminal laws could be ex post facto laws. Neither did the statute unconstitutionally impair any contractual obligation because there was a good reason for the law, i.e., to record possible clouds on title. Neither did the statute effect a taking. Although it effectively extinguished the landowner's successors' rights in the land, it was not done for public use. Finally, the statute was not unconstitutionally retroactive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the railroad's successors.

 

961 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wolfs


CA No. A60331


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


105 Ore. App. 5; 803 P.2d 1192; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 1757


August 15, 1990, Argued and submitted  
December 26, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 27, 1991. Petition for Review Allowed April 2, 1991 (311 Or 261).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. F. Gordon Cottrell, Judge. No. 10-88-01844.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which convicted defendant of being an ex-convict in possession of a firearm. Defendant contended that the trial court erred by denying his motion to dismiss on former jeopardy grounds.


OVERVIEW: At his first trial, after the State had rested, defendant moved for a judgment of acquittal on the ground that the indictment did not set out facts sufficient to establish a crime. The trial court granted the motion and issued an order acquitting defendant but giving the State leave to resubmit the case. The State resubmitted the case and obtained a new indictment. At the trial on the new indictment, defendant moved for dismissal on the basis of former jeopardy, arguing that the previous acquittal barred the second prosecution for the same offense. The court agreed that the granting of a motion for judgment of acquittal on the grounds that the indictment did not set out facts sufficient to establish a crime barred a subsequent prosecution for the same offense. Had defendant demurred to the original indictment, the granting of his motion would not have raised a former jeopardy bar. Controlling Oregon case law prohibited the court from treating defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal as a demurrer. As defendant was acquitted after jeopardy had attached, his second prosecution was barred by the Oregon Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment convicting defendant, holding that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss.

 

962 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Borisoff v. Workers' Compensation Bd.


CA No. A60630 (control), CA No. A60631, CA No. A60632 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


104 Ore. App. 603; 802 P.2d 98; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 1673


September 24, 1990, Submitted on record and briefs  
December 12, 1990  
December 12, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 21, 1990. Second Correction.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Duane R. Ertsgaard, Judge. Nos. 88C-11352, 88C-11350, 88C-11323.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated mandamus proceedings to compel respondent, the Oregon Workers' Compensation Board, to exercise its own motion jurisdiction to increase their permanent disability awards, relator injured workers challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which, in each case, issued an alternative writ of mandamus but dismissed the writ after considering its merits.


OVERVIEW: The workers suffered compensable injuries. After the expiration of their respective aggravation rights under Or. Rev. Stat. § 656.273, each petitioned the Board to exercise its own motion jurisdiction and award him additional permanent disability benefits due to the worsening of his condition. The Board refused to consider the requests and held that § 656.278 did not permit it to award permanent disability benefits on its own motion. The workers sued in mandamus. The circuit court denied relief. The Board acted properly. The workers argued that because it no longer permitted own motion review of permanent disability, § 656.278 violated Or. Const. art. I, § 10. The imposition of limitations on the bringing of a workers' compensation claim did not infringe a claimant's constitutional rights, and it was a permissible legislative function to balance the possibility of outlawing legitimate claims against the public need that at some definite time there be an end to potential litigation. The legislature did not violate the workers' rights under § 10 by eliminating the Board's discretionary jurisdiction to modify permanent disability awards on its own motion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

963 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Peters


CA No. A62574 (Control), CA No. A62575, CA No. A62828, CA No. A62829) (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


104 Ore. App. 582; 801 P.2d 904; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 1683


August 29, 1990, Argued and submitted  
December 12, 1990  
December 12, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Stephen L. Gallagher, Judge. Nos. C89-01-30399, C89-01-30509, C89-01-30409, C89-01-30511.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which convicted him of nine crimes, orally sentenced him to four concurrent indeterminate terms, not to exceed 10 years, and stated that two of the terms included minimum terms of 2.5 years.


OVERVIEW: After defendant pleaded guilty to nine crimes, the circuit court orally sentenced him to four concurrent indeterminate terms, not to exceed 10 years. Final judgment was delayed, pending defendant's taking a polygraph examination. Defendant was transferred to a state penitentiary. Transport orders did not mention any minimum term. Defendant sought clarification of the sentence, but as he had not then yet taken a polygraph examination, no final judgment had been entered. The circuit court subsequently stated in a hearing that two of the terms included minimum terms of 2.5 years. Final judgments were then prepared and entered. Defendant contended that the trial judge's oral pronouncement did not include a minimum term and that once the sentence had been imposed and he began to serve it, the sentencing court illegally modified his sentence in the written judgment. As defendant pleaded guilty, the appeal was governed by Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050. Because defendant did not claim that the sentence imposed either exceeded the maximum allowed by law or was unconstitutionally cruel and unusual, on direct appeal, the court could not review his assertion of error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Lane County v. State


CA No. A60714


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


104 Ore. App. 372; 801 P.2d 870; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 1588


July 16, 1990, Argued and submitted  
November 21, 1990  
November 21, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 13, 1991. Petition for Review Denied April 16, 1991 (311 Or 266).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Pierre Van Rysselberghe, Judge. No. 16-87-09905.



DISPOSITION: Judgment on fourth counterclaim reversed and remanded; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant investigator sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which granted partial summary judgment to plaintiff county in the county's declaratory judgment action against the investigator and defendant State of Oregon.


OVERVIEW: The investigator, employed by the district attorney's office, suffered an on-the-job injury. He later applied for reinstatement pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 659.415, 659.420, and also applied for a promotion to sergeant. The county refused reinstatement on the ground that the investigator's position had been eliminated, and refused to promote him, contending that a labor agreement required that sergeants belong to the union. The county then filed an action seeking a declaration that the investigator was a state employee. The investigator claimed that he was entitled to reinstatement and that the county's interpretation of the labor agreement violated his equal protection rights. The trial court granted the county partial summary judgment. The investigator appealed. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment in part. The court rejected the reinstatement claim, noting that the county had proved that the investigator was discharged for reasons unrelated to his injury. The court found, however, that ambiguities in the labor agreement, including the scope of the union membership requirement, made summary judgment inappropriate regarding the investigator's application for a promotion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in part and remanded to the trial court.

 

965 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sasser


CA No. A61974


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


104 Ore. App. 251; 799 P.2d 1146; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 1492


June 29, 1990, Argued and submitted  
November 7, 1990  
November 7, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied January 16, 1991. Petition for Review Denied February 5, 1991 (311 Or 151).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Hollie Pihl, Judge. No. C89-0186CR.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged her conviction for escape in the second degree in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.155 by the Circuit Court, Washington County (Oregon).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to serve a term of 60 days in jail on a misdemeanor conviction, and she was released early under a furlough release agreement due to jail overcrowding. Under the furlough release agreement, defendant was released on the condition that she was to have (1) resided at her sister's home, (2) returned to the residence by a certain time each night, and (3) that she was to have reported to the jail three times a week by phone. Defendant's conviction was had on her stipulation that she failed to return to the residence by the designated time on a given date, that she neglected to check in with the jail by phone on three occasions, and that she failed to comply with a deputy's demand that she return to jail. On appeal, the court affirmed. Under § 162.135(2), defendant remained within the custody of the sheriff and was constructively confined to a correctional facility under the terms of her furlough release agreement. Defendant's violation of the furlough release agreement constituted an escape under §§ 162.135(4), 162.155. The mere presence of discretion under the furlough release agreement did not render discriminatory the decision to charge defendant with escape.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction by the trial court.

 

966 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Saunders


CA No. A49948


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


103 Ore. App. 488; 799 P.2d 159; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 1296


June 19, 1989, Argued and submitted; May 9, 1990, Resubmitted In Banc  
October 3, 1990  
October 3, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Wasco County. James C. Donnell, Judge. No. 87-262.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order by the District Court, Wasco County(Oregon)suppressing evidence discovered during a warrantless search of defendant's interstate shipment of a box of sturgeon eggs (roe). It argued that the search was either a statutorily authorized administrative search or it was lawful, because there were probable cause and exigent circumstances.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a licensed wholesale fish dealer. An officer of the Oregon State Police Fish and Game Division suspected that defendant was shipping roe taken from sturgeon longer than the legal limit. The officer was at an airport when he saw a package delivered from defendant's business for shipment. The invoice on the package stated that it contained raw sturgeon eggs. The officer testified that packages of roe were generally shipped from the airport within an hour after receipt. He immediately opened the box, seized its contents, and confirmed by laboratory analysis the next day that the roe came from a single sturgeon skein and that the sturgeon's length exceeded the legal limit.Defendant moved to suppress the evidence, arguing that the officer's warrantless search and seizure was unconstitutional. The trial court granted the motion, and the state appealed. The court agreed with the trial court's conclusion that there was probable cause to justify the search. However, the court also agreed with the trial court that the state had not established that there were exigent circumstances. The state did not show that there was a justification for seizing the package without a warrant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

967 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Merrick v. Board of Higher Educ.


CA No. A60997


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


103 Ore. App. 328; 797 P.2d 388; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 1255


July 31, 1990, Respondents' Motion to Dismiss; August 25, 1990, Respondents' Motion to Strike  
September 5, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Judicial Review of Administrative Rule.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss denied; motion to strike affidavit allowed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, Oregon Board of Higher Education (board) and the State of Oregon, filed a motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction petitioner board employee's Or. Rev. Stat. § 183.400 petition to determine the validity of Or. Admin. R. 580-22-050, Or. Admin. R. 580-15-010, and Or. Admin. R. 580-15-065, which prohibited discrimination based on sexual orientation, in light of Or. Rev. Stat. 236.380(2), which permitted such discrimination.


OVERVIEW: A board employee brought an action against the board and the state under Or. Rev. Stat. § 183.400 to determine the validity of Or. Admin. R. 580-22-050, Or. Admin. R. 580-15-010, and Or. Admin. R. 580-15-065, which were promulgated by the board forbidding discrimination based on sexual orientation. The board and the state filed a motion to dismiss. The court held that the employee was not required to seek a discretionary hearing from the board under Or. Rev. Stat. § 183.410 before filing her petition. The employee's request to uphold the rules necessarily put the question of the rules' validity before the court. Thus, the court had jurisdiction over the petition. Because recently adopted Or. Rev. Stat. § 236.380(2) permitted discrimination based on sexual orientation, because § 236.382(2) was presumed to be constitutional, and because the board and the state declined to take a position in respect to the effect of § 236.382(2) on the rules, a justiciable controversy existed. Therefore, the court denied the motion.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion of the board and the state to dismiss the petition of the board's employee to determine the validity of the board's rules that prohibited discrimination based on sexual orientation in light of an Oregon statute that permitted such discrimination. The court found that it had jurisdiction and that a justiciable controversy existed.

 

968 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Moccio v. Department of Human Resources, Adult & Family Services Div.


CA No. A49591


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


103 Ore. App. 207; 796 P.2d 1233; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 1091


February 26, 1990, Argued and submitted  
August 29, 1990  
August 29, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Judicial Review from Adult and Family Services Division. No. 2-2801-AP5222-9.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner guardian appealed from an order entered by respondent, the Adult and Family Services Division (AFSD), which discontinued Aid to Dependent Children (ADC) to three minor children and denied her application for benefits on behalf of the children.


OVERVIEW: The guardian was appointed after the children's father was incarcerated. Before his incarceration, the father received ADC for himself and the children. The AFSD concluded that the children were not eligible for continued assistance because the guardian did not qualify as a "caretaker relative" under Or. Admin. R. 461-05-410. It also ruled that the denial of benefits was not unconstitutional. The guardian appealed from that decision, which was affirmed. The court rejected her argument that Rule 461-05-410 was more restrictive than the eligibility standards contained in 45 C.F.R. § 233.90(c)(1)(v). In that regard, the guardian, not their father, was responsible for the children's day-to-day care. Therefore, they were also ineligible under § 233.90(c)(1)(v). The AFSD had also provided an adequate explanation for its refusal to waive the eligibility requirements. Furthermore, Or. Admin. R. 461-05-410 did not deprive the children of equal protection. In that regard, the rule's distinction between children who lived with caretaker relatives and those who did not was rationally related the to AFSD's mission under 42 U.S.C.S. § 601 to strengthen families.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the AFSD's order terminating the ADC payments.

 

969 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Moen v. Peterson


CA No. A61667


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


103 Ore. App. 71; 795 P.2d 1109; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 906


June 11, 1990, Argued and submitted  
August 8, 1990  
August 8, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Allowed by Opinion November 28, 1990 See 104 Or App 481, 802 P2d 76 (1991).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Val D. Sloper, Judge. No. 87C-11030.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which denied his petition against respondent State of Oregon for post-conviction relief upon his conviction for sodomy in the first degree in violation of Or. Rev. Sat. § 163.405.


OVERVIEW: The inmate pleaded no contest to a charge of sodomy in the first degree in violation of § 163.405. He subsequently sought post-conviction relief, alleging a substantial denial of his state and federal constitutional rights on the basis of failure of counsel to advise him before he entered his plea that the trial court might impose a minimum sentence of up to 10 years. The circuit court denied his petition and he appealed, contending that his knowledge that some minimum sentence could be imposed was not tantamount to his knowing that a 10 year minimum sentence could be imposed. The court reversed the order, holding that in order to waive knowingly and voluntarily the rights that were forfeited by entering a plea of guilty or no contest, the inmate was required to have been appraised on the full potential exposure to incarceration. The inmate's knowledge, based on the imposition of a different minimum sentence in a different case, did not meet that standard. The inmate's conviction was rendered void by his counsel's failure to advise him of the possibility of a minimum sentence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's order denying an inmate of post-conviction relief.

 

970 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


McGowan v. Lane County Local Government Boundary Com.


CA No. A60365


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


102 Ore. App. 381; 795 P.2d 560; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 687


June 4, 1990, Argued and submitted  
July 18, 1990  
July 18, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 3, 1990. Petition for Review Denied November 20, 1990 (310 Or 612).


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review from Lane County Local Government Boundary Commission. No. 191-00.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owners sought judicial review of a decision from respondent Lane County Local Government Boundary Commission (Oregon), which approved the annexation of intervenor's tract of land into the city pursuant to the expedited procedures provided by Or. Rev. Stat. § 199.466. The property owners asserted that the commission adversely affected their interests in approving the annexation without providing them ample notice and hearing.


OVERVIEW: The property owners land was adjacent to the annexed area, and they maintained that the annexation could adversely affect their interests. They argued that they were not properly notified of the annexation proceedings and were denied an opportunity to be heard. The commission argued that the purpose of the statute was to provide an expedited procedure for annexations. The court confirmed the commission's decision, holding that Or. Rev. Stat. § 199.462(1) enumerated general factors that must be given some consideration before a decision was made; but, it did not articulate specific criteria that a boundary commission was bound to apply as substantive tests in reaching a decision. The court concluded that the property owners' due process arguments also failed because they had no liberty or property interest, or concomitant procedural rights, that originated in the due process clause itself. The court also noted that no due process violations were applicable under Or. Rev. Stat. § 199.463 because it only applied to persons without participatory rights under the other provisions of the statute, and did not enlarge what the other provisions of the statute granted or withheld.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the commission in approving the annexation of the intervenor's land into the city.

 

971 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Klinger v. Morrow County Grain Growers, Inc.


CA No. A62353


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


102 Ore. App. 375; 794 P.2d 811; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 695


May 18, 1990, Argued and submitted  
July 18, 1990  
July 18, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied September 5, 1990. Petition for Review Denied October 2, 1990 (310 Or 422).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Morrow County. Jack F. Olsen, Judge. No. 88-CV-117.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff business owner challenged an order of the Circuit Court, Morrow County (Oregon), dismissing the business owner's unfair competition action brought against defendant competitor under Or. Rev. Stat. § 480.330.


OVERVIEW: The business owner and the competitor both operated gasoline service stations. After the competitor offered self-service, the business owner brought an unfair competition action against him. The trial court dismissed the action for failure to state a claim, and the business owner sought review. The court affirmed, holding that the business owner did not have a cause of action under § 480.330 because the objective of the statute was safety, not the protection of the business owner's business interests. Because the business owner was not a member of the class that the statute was designed to protect, he could not bring an action under the statute. Also, the business owner was not entitled to bring a common law cause of action against the competitor because, without a statutory violation by the competitor, there was no common law cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the business owner's unfair competition action against the competitor.

Elvin v. Oregon Public Employees Union

PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review from Employment Relations Board. UP No. 38-87.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner union sough review of the order of the Employment Relations Board (Oregon), which found that the union committed unfair labor practices and ordered it to reimburse the "fair share" payments that respondent non-member employees had made under the Public Employees Collective Bargaining Act.


OVERVIEW: The union collected mandatory "fair share" payments from the non-member employees. The Board found that the union had violated the safeguards and ordered it to return the payments to the employees. Stat. § 243.676(4). The court reviewed the statute for the legislature's intent and deferred to the agency's interpretation. The court found that the Board's order was consistent with its broad grant of authority to achieve the purpose of the Public Employees Collective Bargaining Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Board, which found that the union committed unfair labor practices and ordered to reimburse the employees.

 

973 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Foland v. Jackson County


CA No. A63989


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


101 Ore. App. 632; 792 P.2d 1228; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 533


April 16, 1990, Argued and submitted  
May 23, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied August 1, 1990. Petition for Review Allowed September 18, 1990 (310 Or 393).


PRIOR HISTORY: Judicial Review from Land Use Board of Appeals. Nos. 89-105 and 89-111.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed on petition and cross-petition; motion requesting judicial notice allowed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizens challenged the decree of the Land Use Board of Appeals (LUBA) in favor of respondent county. The decree permitted respondent landowner to site a destination resort on land that was designated and zoned at that time for exclusive farm use. The citizens contended that Statewide Planning Goal 8 prohibited such a use on land with 50 or more acres of unique farm land as defined by the United States Soil Conservation Service (SCS).


OVERVIEW: The county's decision to permit the landowner to site a destination resort was based upon amendments to the county's comprehensive plan and zoning map. The citizens contended that LUBA erred by not requiring the county to show that the amendments complied with Goal 8 and by permitting the county to base its determination of whether the site contained 50 acres of unique farm on SCS studies and maps that were taken after the original destination resort siting map was made. Determinations based upon such subsequent studies were permitted by the "refinement clause" in the county's plan. Under the county's original destination resort siting map, the land would not qualify. A subsequent SCS study and map found that the site did qualify. The citizens argued that under Goal 8, Or. Rev. Stat. § 197.435 et seq, and county laws the original destination resort map was conclusive; the later SCS maps could not be considered. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that § 197.435 et seq. did not make original plan maps the exclusive means for determining whether the "50 contiguous acres" siting criterion was present in particular cases. The same reasoning applied to Goal 8 compliance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed LUBA's decision. Judicial notice of an agenda and related documents prepared by the Department of Land Conservation and Development was taken at the request of the citizens.

 

974 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Monroe


Nos. 89-60267, CA A60588


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


101 Ore. App. 379; 790 P.2d 1188; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 481


November 20, 1989, Argued and submitted  
April 25, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Lane County. Kip W. Leonard, Judge. No. 89-60267.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the District Court, Lane County (Oregon), which convicted her of failing to perform the duties of a driver under Or. Rev. Stat. § 811.700(1)(a). Defendant contended that the statute was unconstitutional and that the trial court failed to give a requested jury instruction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in an accident that caused damage to another car. She testified that she stopped at the scene, drove across the intersection, and then stopped again. She looked around, did not see the other car, and believed it had left the scene. Other witnesses testified that she stopped only briefly or not at all. Defendant was convicted of failure to perform the duties of a driver. On appeal, she claimed that Or. Rev. Stat. § 811.700(1)(a) violated Or. Const. art. I, § 12, proscribing compulsory self-incrimination. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the statute was not unconstitutional on its face where the remote possibility that the information required by the statute would result in criminal liability was not enough to invoke the privilege against self-incrimination; (2) defendant failed to show that the reporting of her name and address to the other driver would have placed her substantially at risk of incriminating herself; thus, the statute did not violate Or. Const. art. I , §12; (3) however, if defendant reasonably believed she could not comply with the statute, failure to give a requested instruction permitting her to assert such a defense was error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision, which convicted defendant of failure to perform the duties of a driver. The court remanded the cause for a new trial.

 

975 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bichsel


Nos. B70 854, CA A47766


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


101 Ore. App. 257; 790 P.2d 1142; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 450


February 21, 1989, Submitted on record and briefs; December 6, 1989, Resubmitted In Banc  
April 18, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Lane County. Laurie K. Smith, Judge. (Order overruling demurrer.) Winfrid K. Liepe, Judge. (Judgments of February 24, 1988.) No. B70 854.



DISPOSITION: Reversed on conviction for tape recording police radio communication; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the District Court, Lane County (Oregon), which convicted her of tape recording a police radio broadcast without consent of one of the participants in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 165.540(1)(a), and for tape recording a conversation with police officers without specifically informing them in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 165.540(1)(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by a police officer and she had in her possession a police scanner and a tape recorder with which she had been taping police broadcasts. During her encounter she left the tape recorder running and taped the conversation with the police officer. When the officer discovered the recorder he arrested defendant for unlawfully obtaining contents of communications. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred in concluding that the broadcast over the police scanner was not for use by the general public. The court stated that the police had no property or privacy interest in the broadcast and the broadcast was not coded or scrambled. Therefore, the court determined that defendant had not committed any crime when she taped the radio broadcast. However, the court held that defendant violated Or. Rev. Stat. § 165.540(1)(c) when she taped her conversation with the police officer because she failed to give the officer notice that she was taping the conversation. The court reasoned that defendant was aware that the tape recorder was on because tape recording the police broadcast was what brought her to the location at which she was arrested.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for recording the broadcast and affirmed defendant's conviction for recording the face-to-face conversation.

 

976 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reed


Nos. C881415CR, CA A51299


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


101 Ore. App. 277; 790 P.2d 551; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 446


February 28, 1990, Argued and submitted  
April 18, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 13, 1990. Petition for Review Denied July 10, 1990 (310 Or 195).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. Donald C. Ashmanskas, Judge. No. C881415CR.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction for assault with a dangerous weapon in the Circuit Court of Washington County (Oregon) and from the order denying his motion for judgment of acquittal on the ground that a concrete sidewalk was not a "dangerous weapon" within the meaning of Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.015(1). Defendant also contended that his sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant repeatedly struck his girlfriend's head against a concrete sidewalk. He was convicted of assault with a dangerous weapon and sentenced to six years in prison after the trial court denied his motion for judgment of acquittal. Defendant contended that the concrete sidewalk was not a "dangerous weapon" within the meaning of Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.015(1). The court disagreed and affirmed the conviction, holding that denial of the motion for acquittal was not error. Whether defendant forcibly brought a piece of hand-held concrete into contact with the victim's head, or forcibly brought her head into contact with a concrete sidewalk, the concrete was a "dangerous weapon." Under the circumstances in which it was used, the sidewalk was readily capable of causing death or serious physical injury. The court also affirmed the six-year sentence imposed as being lawful and within the maximum allowed by statute. The court did not address defendant's argument that § 161.015(1) was unconstitutionally vague because defendant did not raise the argument in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for assault with a dangerous weapon.

State v. Brungard


Nos. 8804-95-776, CA A48450


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


101 Ore. App. 67; 789 P.2d 683; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 295


October 23, 1989, Argued and submitted  
March 28, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Granted July 18, 1990, Reported at 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 783.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Carol J. Kyle, Judge pro tempore. No. 8804-95-776.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant allegedly mentally ill person sought review of a judgment entered in the Circuit Court for Multnomah County (Oregon) that determined that he was a mentally ill person under Or. Rev. Stat. § 426.005 (2) (b) and committed him for 180 days.


OVERVIEW: The children of the allegedly mentally ill person initiated an action to have him committed. The trial court found that the allegedly mentally ill person was a mentally ill person that was unable to care for his basic needs and met the expanded criteria under Or. Rev. Stat. § 426.005 (2)(c) for commitment based on the allegedly mentally ill person's repeated hospitalizations in the past. On appeal, the allegedly mentally ill person argued that the evidence was not sufficient to support the trial court's ruling and that the statute containing the expanded criteria was unconstitutional and violated the allegedly mentally ill person's due process. The court rejected the allegedly mentally ill person's arguments. The court pointed out that the allegedly mentally ill person was chronically mentally ill as defined by Or. Rev. Stat. § 426.005(2)(c)(A) as he had a long-standing bipolar disorder. The court found that the evidence showed that he had been previously committed, which satisfied Or. Rev. Stat. § 426.005(2)(c)(B). Finally, due process did not require the state to wait until the allegedly mentally ill person tried to take his life before initiating commitment proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that determined that the alleged mentally ill person was a mentally ill person and involuntarily committed him.

State v. Olaiz


CA No. A49378


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


100 Ore. App. 380; 786 P.2d 734; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 78


May 19, 1989, Argued and submitted  
February 7, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 28, 1990. Petition for Review Denied June 5, 1990 (310 Or 122).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Thomas Moultrie, Judge. No. 88-01-30523.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court of Multnomah County (Oregon) for delivery of a controlled substance, assigning as error the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that evidence obtained during a traffic stop for speeding should have been suppressed because the traffic stop was not valid under Or. Rev. Stat. § 810.410 and that it was a "pretext stop" in violation of Or. Const. art. I, § 9 and the Fourth Amendment. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court. It held that despite the fact that the officers did not stop the car immediately after witnessing the speeding infraction, Or. Rev. Stat. § 810.410 did not contain a limitation on the time within which an officer must cite an offending driver. The court also rejected defendant's argument that under the Fourth Amendment, the court should ask whether a reasonable officer would have made the stop absent an improper purpose. The court found this standard unworkable and undesirable requiring the court to decide whether an officer had noticed anything beyond the violation itself and, if so, would have made the stop on the hypothetical supposition that he had noticed something. The same reasoning applied under Or. Const. art. I, § 9, and whether the officers would have stopped defendant for speeding absent their desire to know more about the car's occupants was irrelevant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress evidence of possession of controlled substances obtained during a traffic stop for speeding.

Portland v. Bitans

State v. Cargill


CA Nos. A49496 (Control), A49497, A49498, A49499, A49500, A49501 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


100 Ore. App. 336; 786 P.2d 208; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 73


August 23, 1989, Argued and submitted  
January 31, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 6, 1990. Petition for Review Allowed July 3, 1990 (310 Or 133).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Multnomah County, District Court. Joseph F. Ceniceros, Judge. Nos. DA369633-8805, DA369634-8805, DA369631-8805, DA369632-8805, DA39629-8805, DA369630-8805.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions for criminal trespass in the second degree, under Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.245 entered in the Multnomah County, District Court (Oregon). The district court reduced the charges from Class C misdemeanors to violations, under Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.565(2). Defendants were given a sentence of discharge, under Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 137.010 (7)(d) and 161.715.


OVERVIEW: Defendants stood on the store's private property seeking signatures on several initiative petitions. A store employee, pursuant to company policy, directed defendants to leave. They refused to, which led to their arrests and convictions. Defendants appealed, contending that the order to leave was unconstitutional under Or. Const. arts. I, § 8 and IV, § 1. The state argued that the right did not confer a right of access to private property over the objection of its owner. The court reversed, concluding that the order to leave the store's premises was not lawful and that using it as the foundation for a criminal prosecution improperly interfered with the people's right under art. IV, § 1 to initiate legislation. The court reasoned that the store's premises, by reason of the owner's invitation, became a forum for assembly by the community. Notwithstanding the store's apparent policy against allowing petitioners on its property, there was no evidence that defendants' activities substantially interfered with the store's commercial activity, had a serious economic impact on the store or interfered with its reasonable investment backed expectations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' convictions for criminal trespass for using the store's property to collect signatures on petitions and refusing to leave when so ordered.

Perez v. Coast to Coast Reforestation Corp.

COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


100 Ore. App. 115; 785 P.2d 365; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 19


November 22, 1989, Argued and submitted  
January 17, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Duane R. Ertsgaard, Judge. No. 87C 11014.



DISPOSITION: Dismissal of first, second, seventh and eighth claims for relief reversed and remanded; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff workers sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which dismissed their action against defendant employer for unpaid wages and for penalties and related relief under Or. Rev. Stat. § 652.150 and the Farm Labor Contractors Act, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 658.405-658.485.


OVERVIEW: The employer contended that because the workers performed their services in Idaho, the Oregon statutes were inapplicable. The employer based its arguments on choice of law principles and argued that it would be unconstitutional to apply the statutes extraterritorially. On appeal, the court determined that the action involved employment contracts entered into in Oregon between Oregon workers and Oregon employers. Because Idaho had no statute that corresponded to the Act and the purpose of the Act clearly included the protection of workers and the assurance of their compensation, the court held that the Act applied to the Oregon employment contracts. The court also rejected the employer's argument that Idaho rather than Oregon law should apply to the claims for unpaid wages. Finally, the court rejected the employer's contentions that the complaint failed to state ultimate facts sufficient to constitute a claim against it as the worker's "employer." The court refused to affirm a dismissal on pure pleading grounds because only substantive legal reasons for dismissal were presented to the trial court and an amendment could cure the defect.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment with regard to the claims brought under the Act and claims for unpaid wages and penalties.

Emerald People's Utility Dist. v. Pacificorp


CA No. A49816


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


100 Ore. App. 79; 784 P.2d 1112; 1990 Ore. App. LEXIS 4


July 17, 1989, Argued and submitted  
January 3, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Allowed by Opinion March 21, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Douglas County. Ronald Poole, Judge. No. L87-1282.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff utility district appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Douglas County (Oregon), which denied the utility district's motion to strike the defenses of defendant public utility and intervenor utility commission and dismissed the action brought to condemn four hydroelectric generating plants and related facilities that the public utility owned and operated.


OVERVIEW: The utility district adopted a resolution pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 35.235(1) and then brought an action to condemn four hydroelectric generating plants and related facilities that the public utility owned and operated. The public utility and the intervenor utility commission asserted through affirmative defenses that the proposed condemnation was not most compatible with the greatest public good and the least private injury. The utility district filed a motion to strike the defenses, which the trial court denied. The trial court dismissed the action. The utility district appealed and the court found that the utility district's customers were already served at favorable rates, which would improve still more if the utility district acquired the public utility's power plants. The court found that the benefit to the utility district's customers from that acquisition would be substantially outweighed by the economic detriment to the public utility and its customers, the number of which exceeded the utility district's by many times. The court agreed with the trial court's findings of the underlying facts and the conclusion that the utility district abused its discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the utility district's condemnation action.

 

983 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Atlantic Richfield Co. v. Greene


CA No. A50686


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


100 Ore. App. 16; 784 P.2d 442; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 2110


October 25, 1989, Argued and submitted  
December 28, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 2, 1990. Petition for Review Denied April 26, 1990 (309 Or 698).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Lee Johnson, Judge. No. 8712-07691.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, two individuals, a gasoline supplier, three gasoline retailers, and a self-service gasoline equipment dealer, challenged the decision of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which entered judgment in favor of respondent, the Fire Marshall, in appellants' action for a declaration that Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 480.330, 480. 340, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellants sought a declaration that two statutes, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 480.330, 480.340, which prohibited retail gasoline sellers from permitting customers to dispense their own gasoline, were unconstitutional. Appellants claimed that the statutes granted a privilege to those nonretail sellers to whom the statutes did not apply and thus violated Or. Const. art. I, § 20, and the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. Appellants also claimed that the Commerce Clause was violated. The court disagreed and affirmed. The court held that the distinction between retail and nonretail sellers was a distinction created by the statutory scheme that appellants sought to invalidate. Sellers were free to join whichever "class" they desired and, by electing to be retail sellers, subjected themselves to the applicable statutes. The Equal Protection Clause was not violated because the legislature's conclusion that customers dispensing gasoline was dangerous was rational, even if erroneous. The Commerce Clause did not apply because it was not intended to protect the particular structure or methods of operation in a retail market.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of respondent in appellants' action for a declaration that statutes that prohibited retail gasoline sellers from permitting customers to dispense their own gasoline were unconstitutional.

Oregon Ass'n of Rehabilitation Professionals etc. v. Department of Ins. & Finance


CA No. A47225


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


99 Ore. App. 613; 783 P.2d 1014; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 1974


November 7, 1988, Argued and submitted  
December 13, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Judicial Review from Department of Insurance and Finance. WCD No. 11-1987.



DISPOSITION: Rule held valid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After an administrative rule was held valid, petitioner non-profit vocational corporation sought judicial review of a rule of respondent Oregon Department of Insurance and Finance, specifically Or. Admin. R. 436-120-215, that regulated payments made by insurers to vocational assistance providers who provided services to injured workers.


OVERVIEW: The corporation was a non-profit association of vocational assistance professionals who provided services to injured workers. The corporation contested Or. Admin. R. 436-120-215, which regulated all payments made by insurers or employers to providers and established the maximum amounts that could be paid to providers for specified services and set maximum limits for each worker. The Department held that the rule was valid, and on review, the court agreed. The rule did not exceed the authority granted by Or. Rev. Stat. § 656.340(9)(d), the rule's authorizing statute, because the ability to set maximum fees was inherent in the statute. The rates were based on rates charged by rehabilitation organizations, so the rates were reasonable and within the agency's range of discretion. The rule and statute did not violate Or. Const. art. I, § 20, because any limitation on the right to contract had a direct bearing on the public interest and enabled the Department to carry out the legislative policy of Oregon's worker' compensation law. There was no improper delegation of legislative authority because the sufficient safeguard of reasonable rates was present.


OUTCOME: The rule was held valid.
