In re Adoption of Kyle


CA No. A49713


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


99 Ore. App. 236; 782 P.2d 158; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 1788


October 5, 1989, Argued and submitted  
November 8, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Clackamas County. Richard J. Burke, Senior Judge. No. A87-11-7.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of an order of the Circuit Court, Clackamas County (Oregon), which granted the adoption of his minor son by appellees, a mother and her husband, without his consent and over his objection. The father argued that Or. Rev. Stat. § 109.322, which provided that consent to adoption by an imprisoned parent was not required, conflicted with other statutes and was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The father was in prison serving a sentence of over 20 years for rape, sodomy, and kidnapping. The father had married the mother after the child was born. After she remarried, the mother and the husband sought to adopt the child. The circuit court found that the child's best interests required that the adoption should proceed notwithstanding the father's objections. The father argued that § 109.322 was contrary to Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.275, which provided that convicted felons retained all the rights of the person. He also asserted that Or. Rev. Stat. § 109.322 was unconstitutional because it improperly created an additional punishment for the crimes for which he had been incarcerated. On appeal, the court held that § 109.322 did not conflict with Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.275 because § 137.275 was enacted to reduce secondary sanctions for the commission of felonies whereas Or. Rev. Stat. § 109.322 had been enacted to facilitate the welfare of children whose parents were subject to long-term imprisonment. Because § 109.322 did not penalize an imprisoned parent but rather ameliorated the effect of the parent's long-term incarceration on a child, it was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order.

 

986 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


McIntyre v. Crouch


CA No. A44574


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


98 Ore. App. 462; 780 P.2d 239; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 1096; 83 A.L.R.4th 277


May 18, 1988, Argued and submitted  
September 13, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 9, 1989. Petition for Review Denied November 30, 1989 (308 Or 593).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Jackson County. Mitchell Karaman, Judge. No. 2109-F.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father challenged an order of the Circuit Court, Jackson County (Oregon), which held that respondent mother was entitled to a grant of her cross-motion for summary judgment in the father's action to obtain parental rights regarding a child that was conceived through artificial insemination with the father's sperm.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted the mother's cross-motion for summary judgment in the father's action to be declared the father of an artificially conceived child, determining that Or. Rev. Stat. § 109.239 barred the father from obtaining parental rights. The court reversed that grant on appeal and remanded the case. The court found that the plain language of § 109.239, which denied parental rights to donors whose semen was used to conceive a child, showed that it applied to the father because there was no indication of legislative intent to not apply § 109.239 simply because the donor was not anonymous. The court also held that § 109.239, as it applied to the father, did not violate the state constitution due to that statute's rational connection with a legislative aim of facilitating artificial insemination by unmarried women. The court further determined that § 109.239, as applied to the father, would have violated the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment if he established that he donated his semen in reliance on an agreement to give him the rights and responsibilities of fatherhood because that would have shown that he chose to participate in his child's rearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a grant of the mother's cross-motion for summary judgment.

 

987 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Portland v. Levi


CA No. A50617


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


98 Ore. App. 341; 779 P.2d 192; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 1063


June 12, 1989, Argued and submitted  
September 6, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Allowed by Opinion January 31, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Multnomah County. Marshall Amiton, Judge. No. DA360279.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction by the District Court, Multnomah County (Oregon) for loitering to solicit prostitution, a violation of Portland, Or., City Code § 14.24.050(b). Claiming the evidence was insufficient, defendant assigned as error the trial court's denial of her motions for judgment of acquittal and arrest of judgment. She contended that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague under Or. Const. art. I, §§ 20 and 21.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance made it unlawful to loiter near a street under circumstances, including beckoning to or attempting to stop drivers, that manifested a purpose of soliciting to commit an act of prostitution. A police officer observed defendant standing with two other women near a street corner in an area that the officer characterized as a "high vice area." The officer told the women to move on, but defendant and one companion got in a pickup truck that had pulled up to the curb. Defendant argued on appeal that the evidence did not prove her guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that defendant's activity, taken together with her previous admission to the officer that she was a prostitute, afforded a sufficient basis for a trier of fact to find beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant had violated the ordinance. The court stated that it had previously upheld the constitutionality of the ordinance against a void-for-vagueness federal constitutional attack. Affirming, the court concluded that the ordinance was not vague under Or. Const. art. I, §§ 20 and 21 because a person could, with reasonable certainty, determine the specific conduct prohibited by the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

Van Lue v. Collins


CA No. A49938


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


98 Ore. App. 140; 779 P.2d 163; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 1037


May 17, 1989, Argued and submitted  
August 30, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Allowed by Opinion November 22, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Milo Pope, Judge. No. 88C 40347.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, petitioners seeking to adopt an infant, challenged a decision of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which denied their motion to dismiss an objection, declared that respondent objector was the child's father, and awarded him custody.


OVERVIEW: A child was conceived while her parents lived together in Maine. The mother then returned to her family in Oregon and refused to respond to the objector's offers to contribute to the child's support, including a $ 200 check that was returned in an unopened letter. When the mother learned that the objector was travelling to Oregon, she filed an affidavit stating that the objector was the putative father but that he had not contributed to or tried to contribute to the child's support, and placed the child with the petitioners for adoption. The objector opposed the adoption, stating that he was still willing to care for the child and desired custody. The petitioners alleged that it was error to allow the objection to adoption because the objector was not a party entitled to notice and the evidence of attempts to support the child was insufficient. In affirming the decision, the court held that the objector was entitled to notice under Or. Rev. Stat. § 109.096(1)(b) and therefore was entitled to object to the adoption proceeding pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 109.098(1). The trial court had correctly denied the adoption petition and awarded custody to the objector-father.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order declaring that the objector was the father and awarding him custody of the child.

State v. Knobel


CA No. A43491


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


97 Ore. App. 559; 777 P.2d 985; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 867; 16 Media L. Rep. 2478


February 22, 1989, Argued and submitted  
July 19, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied January 5, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Josephine County. Allan H. Coon, Judge. No. 86-454-M.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the District Court of Josephine County (Oregon), which convicted him of unlawfully and knowingly obtaining and attempting to obtain a conversation by use of a tape recorder in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 165.540(1)(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 165.540(1)(c) was unconstitutional because it was overbroad and vague in violation of Or. Const. art. I, § 8 and the First and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution. Defendant also argued that it was error to have refused to admit evidence of the bias of the victim. The court reversed the conviction and remanded the case for a new trial. The court concluded that Or. Rev. Stat. § 165.540(1)(c) was not overbroad or vague under either the Oregon Constitution or the United States Constitution. The court reasoned that the statute was not overbroad because it did not interfere with defendant's right to gather news or his "freedom of the press." The court found that the statute was not vague because it defined the offense in terms such that a person could have determined the specific conduct that would fall within its reach to a reasonable degree of certainty. The court opined, however, that by prohibiting defendant's inquiry on cross-examination regarding the victim's alleged bias, the lower court denied the jury an adequate opportunity to assess the victim's credibility, which resulted in reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for unlawfully and knowingly obtaining and attempting to obtain a conversation by use of a tape recorder and remanded the cause for a new trial.

 

990 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Handran


CA No. A48022


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


97 Ore. App. 546; 777 P.2d 981; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 872


February 28, 1989, Argued and submitted  
July 19, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied August 25, 1989. Petition for Review Denied October 3, 1989 (308 Or 405).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Edwin E. Allen, Judge. No. 10-87-03818.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state challenged the order of the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which suppressed evidence seized by the police without a warrant while searching defendant's apartment for another suspect.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with theft in the first degree in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.055. The state appealed the trial court's order suppressing evidence seized by the police without a warrant while searching defendant's apartment for another suspect. On appeal, the state argued that the seizure was valid under the "plain view" doctrine. Defendant contended that the seizure of the stereo equipment without a warrant or exigent circumstances violated U.S. Const. Art. I, § 9 and the Fourth Amendment. The court reversed. The court held that, if an officer was where he has a right to be, under either a warrant or an exception to the warrant requirement, he might have seized anything that he discovered, if the requirements of Or. Rev. Stat. § 133.585 were met. The officer did no more than what a warrant would have authorized him to do. Contrary to defendant's argument, the officer did not have to "know" that the property was stolen. Or. Rev. Stat. § 135.585 required only that the officer had probable cause. Probable cause did not require certainty.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment suppressing the evidence in question.

Baldwin v. Psychiatric Sec. Review Bd.


CA No. A48172


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


97 Ore. App. 367; 776 P.2d 577; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 764


November 30, 1988, Argued and submitted  
June 28, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Judicial Review from Psychatric Security Review Board. No. 82-487.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner patient sought review of an order of the Psychiatric Security Review Board (Oregon) (PSRB), which denied her request to be discharged or conditionally released under Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.341(4) and continued her 1982 commitment to the state hospital. The issues were whether Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.295(2) (as amended 1983) applied and whether the PSRB erred in finding that she could not be adequately controlled on conditional release.


OVERVIEW: In 1982, petitioner was found not responsible for first degree manslaughter by reason of mental disease or defect. Upon commitment, she was diagnosed as suffering from "mixed personality disorder." The 1983 amendment of § 161.295(2) excluded personality disorders from the terms "mental disease or defect." On appeal, the court held that, read in context, the legislature intended that, before being discharged under Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.341(4)(a), a person could no longer be affected by the mental disease or defect that originally caused him or her to be placed under PSRB's jurisdiction. Petitioner had been committed because she had a mental disease or defect that made her dangerous to others. She still had that malady and was still dangerous to others. Section 161.295(2) did not require her discharge. The court also rejected her claim that that Or. Admin. R. 859-10-005(4)(b) violated the equal treatment guarantees under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Or. Const. art. I, § 20. The two classes of individuals posited by petitioner were not similarly situated. Finally, substantial evidence supported PSRB's finding that petitioner could not adequately be controlled on conditional release.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

993 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smoot


CA No. A47755


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


97 Ore. App. 255; 775 P.2d 344; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 719


April 24, 1989, Argued and submitted  
June 14, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Lane County. Winfrid K. Liepe, Judge. No. B68-696.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the District Court, Lane County (Oregon), which convicted him of carrying a concealed weapon, a switchblade knife, in his trouser pocket in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.240.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of carrying a concealed weapon, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.240. On appeal, he claimed that the statute was unconstitutional because historically knives were carried in trouser pockets and because a switchblade was a modern version of the type of knife that was carried at the time of the adoption of Or. Const. art. I, § 27. The court affirmed, holding that Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.240(1) provided that any person who carried concealed upon the person any knife having a blade that projected or swung into position by force of a spring or by centrifugal force and commonly known as a switchblade knife committed a Class B misdemeanor. Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.240(1) did not impinge on the constitutional right to possess a switchblade knife. A person could possess and carry a switchblade so long as it was not concealed. In light of the historical perspective, and because the legislative encroachment on the right to bear arms was reasonably related to public safety and interfered only with the manner of possession, and not possession itself, the court held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.240(1) did not violate Or. Const. art. I, § 27.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for carrying a concealed weapon, a switchblade knife, in his trouser pocket.

State ex rel. Juvenile Dep't v. Geist


CA No. A45355


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


97 Ore. App. 10; 775 P.2d 843; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 726


September 28, 1988, Argued and submitted; February 14, 1989, Resubmitted In Banc  
June 14, 1989

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Kristena A. LaMar, Judge. Nos. 86518, 86518A, 86518B.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which terminated her parental rights in a proceeding initiated by appellee, the State of Oregon.


OVERVIEW: The mother's husband abused her and the children. After the mother left the home and the father was imprisoned for a sexual abuse conviction, the children were placed in the temporary custody of the Children's Services Division. A reunification plan was formulated, but the mother failed to comply with the plan and her parental rights were terminated. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that there was clear and convincing evidence justifying the termination of the mother's parental rights. The court noted that the mother had psychological problems, that she was reluctant to seek treatment, and that her reluctance to seek treatment interfered with her ability to care for the children. The court also noted that the mother neglected the children's medical and nutritional needs. The court concluded, in light of the fact that the mother had rejected counseling and other efforts to assist her in becoming a fit parent, that there was no realistic chance that the children could safely be returned to her. The court thus found that termination was appropriate. The court also found that the mother could not raise an ineffective assistance of counsel claim on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State ex rel. Juvenile Dep't of Marion County v. Randall


CA No. A48545


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


96 Ore. App. 673; 773 P.2d 1348; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 654


March 24, 1989, Argued and submitted  
May 24, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Albin W. Norblad, Judge. Nos. 29,234, 29,293.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the State of Oregon, through the Juvenile Department of Marion County and Children's Services Division, filed a petition seeking to designate appellant mother's child a ward of the court. The mother sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which made her five-year-old daughter a ward of the trial court, asserting error in its denial of her motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The mother asserted that the petition failed to state sufficient facts to support jurisdiction. The petition alleged that the child was within the jurisdiction of the circuit court by reason that the behavior, condition, or circumstances of the child was such as to endanger the child's own welfare and the welfare of others by reason of the following facts: (1) the child's mother used controlled substances and (2) the child's sibling had controlled substances in her system. The State asserted that a mother's use of controlled substances was a proper consideration in determined if the welfare of the child was endangered. The court reversed the circuit court's judgment. The court found that the petition must have included some factual allegation showing how the parent's drug usage endangered the welfare of the child over whom the court was asserting jurisdiction. It failed to allege that the child's welfare was endangered in any way by mother's drug use. The court reasoned that the fact that a sibling was born with drugs in her system addressed only her welfare and not that of the child in issue. Thus, the allegations were insufficient to establish jurisdiction over the child.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court, which made the mother's five-year-old daughter a ward of the circuit court.

State v. Gerrish


CA No. A46559


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


96 Ore. App. 582; 773 P.2d 793; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 614


July 15, 1988, Argued and submitted  
May 17, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 14, 1989. Petition for Review Allowed August 29, 1989 (308 Or 315).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Lincoln County. Robert J. Huckleberry, Judge. No. CR8702424.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Oregon appealed a judgment of the District Court, Lincoln County (Oregon), which granted defendant's pre-trial motion to suppress evidence obtained during a police roadblock, which evidence was used to convict him of driving under the influence of intoxicants.


OVERVIEW: Police officers set up a roadblock to check vehicles coming from a private lodge where an armed robbery and shooting had occurred. When the officers stopped defendant's automobile, they discovered that he was intoxicated, and they arrested him for driving while intoxicated. Defendant filed a motion to suppress, which the trial court granted on the ground that the roadblock violated Or. Const. art. I, § 9. The State appealed. The court reversed and remanded for a trial, finding that defendant's right were not violated by the stop. The court found that the primary purpose of the roadblock was to apprehend the suspect of a crime, and the secondary purpose was to speak with each driver coming from the scene of the crime to determine whether any of them had witnessed the shooing or robbery. According, the roadblock in the present case clearly was designed to accomplish the broad purposes of Or. Rev. Stat. § 181.030, which authorized the State Police to pursue and apprehend offenders and obtain legal evidence necessary to insure the conviction in the courts of offenders. The procedures in the present case did not invade the constitutional freedoms protected from government interference.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

State v. Cox


CA No. A49180


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


96 Ore. App. 473; 772 P.2d 1385; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 554


February 15, 1989, Argued and submitted  
May 10, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 28, 1989. Petition for Review Denied August 29, 1989 (308 Or 315).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. J. Gordon Cottrell, Judge. No. 10-87-02500.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which convicted him of the unauthorized use of a motor vehicle in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.135.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who had an extensive criminal record, was working as a police informant during several burglary investigations. The police provided defendant with a car for use in the investigation of stolen guns. The car contained a tracking device. At no time did police give defendant permission to take the car out of town, nor did they place specific limits on his use of the car. Defendant called the suspect to arrange a sale of the guns to undercover officers. The sale never occurred because defendant picked up a third person outside of town and let him drive the car, which was pulled over for speeding. Defendant was then convicted of the unauthorized use of a motor vehicle in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.135. On appeal, the court held that: (1) Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.135(1)(a) prohibited both the taking and unauthorized use of a vehicle, (2) there existed sufficient evidence to allow a jury to find that defendant did not have permission to leave town with the car, and (3) defendant's decision to drive out of town to pick up a third person not involved with the investigation allowed the police to decide that he had abandoned his role in the investigation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for unauthorized use of a motor vehicle.

Guard Pub. Co. v. Lane County School Dist.


CA No. A48087


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


96 Ore. App. 463; 774 P.2d 494; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 555; 16 Media L. Rep. 1840


November 21, 1988, Argued and submitted  
May 10, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 30, 1989. Petition for Review Allowed September 19, 1989 (308 Or 382).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Douglas R. Spencer, Judge. No. 16-87-04186.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed on appeal and on cross-appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff publisher brought suit against defendant school district in the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), seeking a declaration that, during a strike, names and addresses of replacement coaches were public records. The trial court agreed as the names, but held that the addresses were exempt from disclosure under Or. Rev. Stat. § 192.502(2), and denied publisher attorney fees. Publisher appealed, and school district cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected school district's contention that coaches' names were exempt from disclosure under Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 192.502(2), 192.502(3), 192.502(8) and 342.850(7). One's name was unquestionably information normally shared with strangers, and teaching and coaching staff in public schools were not anonymous or entitled to be. Coaches' names were not personal nor confidential, even though the information was in their personnel files. The court agreed with the trial court that the coaches' addresses were exempt personal information under Or. Rev. Stat. § 192.502(2), in part because the coaches had submitted the information to the school district in confidence. Under Or. Rev. Stat. § 192.490(3), the trial court had discretion as to whether or not to award attorney's fees because publisher had prevailed only in part, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in failing to award attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

State v. Crocker


CA No. A46952


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


96 Ore. App. 111; 771 P.2d 1026; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 390


May 27, 1988, Argued and submitted  
April 12, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Coos County. Richard L. Barron, Judge. Nos. 87-CR-1724, 87-CR-1725.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court, Coos County (Oregon), which imposed certain conditions on his sentence following his plea of guilty to rape in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to rape in the second degree, involving his having repeated sexual intercourse with his stepdaughter, who was under the age of 14. In granting him probation, the trial court imposed a condition that he not be present in any private residence or vehicle in which there were children under the age of 18. He appealed, and the court, believing that Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050 governed appeals after a defendant pleaded guilty, dismissed the appeal. Following a supreme court decision that the controlling statute was actually Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.040, the court undertook consideration of the appeal on its merits. Defendant's only contention was that the challenged condition should have been more narrowly drawn to provide that he not be present in any private residence or vehicle with a female under the age of 18 without an adult present. The court disagreed, noting that defendant had a history of sexual abuse that may have involved other children and that the presence of adults had little deterrent effect on his sexual conduct in the past. The court concluded that the condition was authorized by Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.540(2)(g)(C).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1000 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Northwest Advancement v. State


CA Nos. A41042 (Control), A41109 (Cases consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


96 Ore. App. 133; 772 P.2d 934; 1989 Ore. App. LEXIS 393; 29 Wage & Hour Cas. (BNA) 433; 122 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P56,915


May 23, 1988, Argued and submitted  
April 12, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 14, 1989. Petition for Review Denied August 29, 1989 (308 Or 315).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from Circuit Court, Marion County, and Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Duane R. Ertsgaard and Stephen B. Herrell, Judges. Marion County No. 85-1052; Multnomah County No. 8601-00401.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, wholesale distributor, its president and sole shareholder, and guardian ad litem, challenged the judgments of the Marion County Circuit Court and the Multnomah County Circuit Court (Oregon) which held in favor of respondents, State of Oregon and parents, upholding the validity of regulations on the employment of minors and granting an injunction requiring the distributor to comply with the regulations.


OVERVIEW: The distributor sold candy and household products through door-to-door sales by minors. The state promulgated regulations of such employment of minors. Appellants filed one action for a declaratory judgment that the regulations were invalid, and the state filed another action seeking injunctions requiring the distributor to comply. The trial courts entered summary judgment that the regulations were valid and issued the injunction. On consolidated appeal, the court affirmed both judgments. The court held that the minors were "employees" under Or. Rev. Stat. § 653.305, whether federal or common law applied. The legislature authorized prohibiting the employment of minors under age 16 as door-to-door salespersons. The regulations did not violate free speech rights because they did not prohibit all solicitation at any time, the government had a substantial interest in the working conditions of minors, and the regulations advanced that interest. The regulations did not violate equal protection rights because the classification was not based on immutable characteristics. An exemption for newspaper carriers had a rational basis. The state had authority to seek injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment that the regulations promulgated by the state governing the use of minors in door-to-door candy sales were valid, and affirmed the grant of the injunction requiring appellants to comply with the regulations.
